I grew more confused each day, more fantastical,\r\nmore supersensual. All the time a beautiful ideal woman hovered in my\r\nimagination. Every so and so often she appeared before me like a vision\r\namong my leather-bound books and dead bones, lying on a bed of roses,\r\nsurrounded by cupids. Sometimes she appeared gowned like the Olympians\r\nwith the stern white face of the plaster Venus; sometimes in braids of\r\na rich brown, blue-eyes, in my aunt\xe2\x80\x99s red velvet _kazabaika,_ trimmed\r\nwith ermine.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cOne morning when she had again risen out of the golden mist of my\r\nimagination in all her smiling beauty, I went to see Countess Sobol,\r\nwho received me in a friendly, even cordial manner. She gave me a kiss\r\nof welcome, which put all my senses in a turmoil. She was probably\r\nabout forty years old, but like most well-preserved women of the world,\r\nstill very attractive. She wore as always her fur-edged jacket. This\r\ntime it was one of green velvet with brown marten. But nothing of the\r\nsternness which had so delighted me the other time was now discernable.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cOn the contrary, there was so little of cruelty in her that without\r\nany more ado she let me adore her.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cOnly too soon did she discover my supersensual folly and innocence,\r\nand it pleased her to make me happy. As for myself\xe2\x80\x94I was as happy as a\r\nyoung god. What rapture for me to be allowed to lie before her on my\r\nknees, and to kiss her hands, those with which she had scourged me!\r\nWhat marvellous hands they were, of beautiful form, delicate, rounded,\r\nand white, with adorable dimples! I really was in love with her hands\r\nonly. I played with them, let them submerge and emerge in the dark fur,\r\nheld them against the light, and was unable to satiate my eyes with\r\nthem.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nWanda involuntarily looked at her hand; I noticed it, and had to smile.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cFrom the way in which the supersensual predominated in me in those\r\ndays you can see that I was in love only with the cruel lashes I\r\nreceived from my aunt; and about two years later when I paid court to a\r\nyoung actress only in the roles she played. Still later I became the\r\nadmirer of a respectable woman. She acted the part of irreproachable\r\nvirtue, only in the end to betray me with a rich Jew. You see, it is\r\nbecause I was betrayed, sold, by a woman who feigned the strictest\r\nprinciples and the highest ideals, that I hate that sort of poetical,\r\nsentimental virtue so intensely. Give me rather a woman who is honest\r\nenough to say to me: I am a Pompadour, a Lucretia Borgia, and I am\r\nready to adore her.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nWanda rose and opened the window.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYou have a curious way of arousing one\xe2\x80\x99s imagination, stimulating all\r\none\xe2\x80\x99s nerves, and making one\xe2\x80\x99s pulses beat faster. You put an aureole\r\non vice, provided only if it is honest. Your ideal is a daring\r\ncourtesan of genius. Oh, you are the kind of man who will corrupt a\r\nwoman to her very last fiber.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n*       *       *       *       *\r\n\r\nIn the middle of the night there was a knock at my window; I got up,\r\nopened it, and was startled. Without stood \xe2\x80\x9cVenus in Furs,\xe2\x80\x9d just as she\r\nhad appeared to me the first time.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYou have disturbed me with your stories; I have been tossing about in\r\nbed, and can\xe2\x80\x99t go to sleep,\xe2\x80\x9d she said. \xe2\x80\x9cNow come and stay with me.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cIn a moment.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nAs I entered Wanda was crouching by the fireplace where she had kindled\r\na small fire.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cAutumn is coming,\xe2\x80\x9d she began, \xe2\x80\x9cthe nights are really quite cold\r\nalready. I am afraid you may not like it, but I can\xe2\x80\x99t put off my furs\r\nuntil the room is sufficiently warm.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cNot like it\xe2\x80\x94you are joking\xe2\x80\x94you know\xe2\x80\x94\xe2\x80\x9d I threw my arm around her, and\r\nkissed her.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cOf course, I know, but why this great fondness for furs?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI was born with it,\xe2\x80\x9d I replied. \xe2\x80\x9cI already had it as a child.\r\nFurthermore furs have a stimulating effect on all highly organized\r\nnatures. This is due both to general and natural laws. It is a physical\r\nstimulus which sets you tingling, and no one can wholly escape it.\r\nScience has recently shown a certain relationship between electricity\r\nand warmth; at any rate, their effects upon the human organism are\r\nrelated. The torrid zone produces more passionate characters, a heated\r\natmosphere stimulation. Likewise with electricity. This is the reason\r\nwhy the presence of cats exercises such a magic influence upon\r\nhighly-organized men of intellect. This is why these long-tailed Graces\r\nof the animal kingdom, these adorable, scintillating electric batteries\r\nhave been the favorite animal of a Mahommed, Cardinal Richelieu,\r\nCrebillon, Rousseau, Wieland.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cA woman wearing furs, then,\xe2\x80\x9d cried Wanda, \xe2\x80\x9cis nothing else than a\r\nlarge cat, an augmented electric battery?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cCertainly,\xe2\x80\x9d I replied. \xe2\x80\x9cThat is my explanation of the symbolic meaning\r\nwhich fur has acquired as the attribute of power and beauty. Monarchs\r\nand the dominant higher nobility in former times used it in this sense\r\nfor their costume, exclusively; great painters used it only for queenly\r\nbeauty. The most beautiful frame, which Raphael could find for the\r\ndivine forms of Fornarina and Titian for the roseate body of his\r\nbeloved, was dark furs.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThanks for the learned discourse on love,\xe2\x80\x9d said Wanda, \xe2\x80\x9cbut you\r\nhaven\xe2\x80\x99t told me everything. You associate something entirely individual\r\nwith furs.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cCertainly,\xe2\x80\x9d I cried. \xe2\x80\x9cI have repeatedly told you that suffering has a\r\npeculiar attraction for me. Nothing can intensify my passion more than\r\ntyranny, cruelty, and especially the faithlessness of a beautiful\r\nwoman. And I cannot imagine this woman, this strange ideal derived from\r\nan aesthetics of ugliness, this soul of Nero in the body of a Phryne,\r\nexcept in furs.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI understand,\xe2\x80\x9d Wanda interrupted. \xe2\x80\x9cIt gives a dominant and imposing\r\nquality to a woman.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cNot only that,\xe2\x80\x9d I continued. \xe2\x80\x9cYou know I am _supersensual._ With me\r\neverything has its roots in the imagination, and thence it receives its\r\nnourishment. I was already pre-maturely developed and highly sensitive,\r\nwhen at about the age of ten the legends of the martyrs fell into my\r\nhands. I remember reading with a kind of horror, which really was\r\nrapture, of how they pined in prisons, were laid on the gridiron,\r\npierced with arrows, boiled in pitch, thrown to wild animals, nailed to\r\nthe cross, and suffered the most horrible torment with a kind of joy.\r\nTo suffer and endure cruel torture from then on seemed to me exquisite\r\ndelight, especially when it was inflicted by a beautiful woman, for\r\never since I can remember all poetry and everything demonic was for me\r\nconcentrated in woman. I literally carried the idea into a sort of\r\ncult.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI felt there was something sacred in sex; in fact, it was the only\r\nsacred thing. In woman and her beauty I saw something divine, because\r\nthe most important function of existence\xe2\x80\x94the continuation of the\r\nspecies\xe2\x80\x94is her vocation. To me woman represented a personification of\r\nnature, _Isis_, and man was her priest, her slave. In contrast to him\r\nshe was cruel like nature herself who tosses aside whatever has served\r\nher purposes as soon as she no longer has need for it. To him her\r\ncruelties, even death itself, still were sensual raptures.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI envied King Gunther whom the mighty Brunhilde fettered on the bridal\r\nnight, and the poor troubadour whom his capricious mistress had sewed\r\nin the skins of wolves to have him hunted like game. I envied the\r\nKnight Ctirad whom the daring Amazon Scharka craftily ensnared in a\r\nforest near Prague, and carried to her castle Divin, where, after\r\nhaving amused herself a while with him, she had him broken on the\r\nwheel\xe2\x80\x94\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cDisgusting,\xe2\x80\x9d cried Wanda. \xe2\x80\x9cI almost wish you might fall into the hands\r\nof a woman of their savage race. In the wolf\xe2\x80\x99s skin, under the teeth of\r\nthe dogs, or upon the wheel, you would lose the taste for your kind of\r\npoetry.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cDo you think so? I hardly do.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cHave you actually lost your senses.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cPossibly. But let me go on. I developed a perfect passion for reading\r\nstories in which the extremest cruelties were described. I loved\r\nespecially to look at pictures and prints which represented them. All\r\nthe sanguinary tyrants that ever occupied a throne; the inquisitors who\r\nhad the heretics tortured, roasted, and butchered; all the woman whom\r\nthe pages of history have recorded as lustful, beautiful, and violent\r\nwomen like Libussa, Lucretia Borgia, Agnes of Hungary, Queen Margot,\r\nIsabeau, the Sultana Roxolane, the Russian Czarinas of last century\xe2\x80\x94all\r\nthese I saw in furs or in robes bordered with ermine.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cAnd so furs now rouse strange imaginings in you,\xe2\x80\x9d said Wanda, and\r\nsimultaneously she began to drape her magnificent fur-cloak\r\ncoquettishly about her, so that the dark shining sable played\r\nbeautifully around her bust and arms. \xe2\x80\x9cWell, how do you feel now, half\r\nbroken on the wheel?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nHer piercing green eyes rested on me with a peculiar mocking\r\nsatisfaction. Overcome by desire, I flung myself down before her, and\r\nthrew my arms about her.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYes\xe2\x80\x94you have awakened my dearest dream,\xe2\x80\x9d I cried. \xe2\x80\x9cIt has slept long\r\nenough.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cAnd this is?\xe2\x80\x9d She put her hand on my neck.\r\n\r\nI was seized with a sweet intoxication under the influence of this warm\r\nlittle hand and of her regard, which, tenderly searching, fell upon me\r\nthrough her half-closed lids.\r\n\r\n_\xe2\x80\x9cTo be the slave of a woman, a beautiful woman, whom I love, whom I\r\nworship.\xe2\x80\x9d_\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cAnd who on that account maltreats you,\xe2\x80\x9d interrupted Wanda, laughing.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYes, who fetters me and whips me, treads me underfoot, the while she\r\ngives herself to another.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cAnd who in her wantonness will go so far as to make a present of you\r\nto your successful rival when driven insane by jealousy you must meet\r\nhim face to face, who will turn you over to his absolute mercy. Why\r\nnot? This final tableau doesn\xe2\x80\x99t please you so well?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nI looked at Wanda frightened.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYou surpass my dreams.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYes, we women are inventive,\xe2\x80\x9d she said, \xe2\x80\x9ctake heed, when you find your\r\nideal, it might easily happen, that she will treat you more cruelly\r\nthan you anticipate.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI am afraid that I have already found my ideal!\xe2\x80\x9d I exclaimed, burying\r\nmy burning face in her lap.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cNot I?\xe2\x80\x9d exclaimed Wanda, throwing off her furs and moving about the\r\nroom laughing. She was still laughing as I went downstairs, and when I\r\nstood musing in the yard, I still heard her peals of laughter above.\r\n\r\n*       *       *       *       *\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cDo you really then expect me to embody your ideal?\xe2\x80\x9d Wanda asked\r\narchly, when we met in the park to-day.\r\n\r\nAt first I could find no answer. The most antagonistic emotions were\r\nbattling within me. In the meantime she sat down on one of the\r\nstone-benches, and played with a flower.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWell\xe2\x80\x94am I?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nI kneeled down and seized her hands.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cOnce more I beg you to become my wife, my true and loyal wife; if you\r\ncan\xe2\x80\x99t do that then become the embodiment of my ideal, absolutely,\r\nwithout reservation, without softness.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYou know I am ready at the end of a year to give you my hand, if you\r\nprove to be the man I am seeking,\xe2\x80\x9d Wanda replied very seriously, \xe2\x80\x9cbut I\r\nthink you would be more grateful to me if through me you realized your\r\nimaginings. Well, which do you prefer?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI believe that everything my imagination has dreamed lies latent in\r\nyour personality.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYou are mistaken.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI believe,\xe2\x80\x9d I continued, \xe2\x80\x9cthat you enjoy having a man wholly in your\r\npower, torturing him\xe2\x80\x94\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cNo, no,\xe2\x80\x9d she exclaimed quickly, \xe2\x80\x9cor perhaps\xe2\x80\x94.\xe2\x80\x9d She pondered.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI don\xe2\x80\x99t understand myself any longer,\xe2\x80\x9d she continued, \xe2\x80\x9cbut I have a\r\nconfession to make to you. You have corrupted my imagination and\r\ninflamed my blood. I am beginning to like the things you speak of. The\r\nenthusiasm with which you speak of a Pompadour, a Catherine the Second,\r\nand all the other selfish, frivolous, cruel women, carries me away and\r\ntakes hold of my soul. It urges me on to become like those women, who\r\nin spite of their vileness were slavishly adored during their lifetime\r\nand still exert a miraculous power from their graves.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYou will end by making of me a despot in miniature, a domestic\r\nPompadour.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWell then,\xe2\x80\x9d I said in agitation, \xe2\x80\x9cif all this is inherent in you, give\r\nway to this trend of your nature. Nothing half-way. If you can\xe2\x80\x99t be a\r\ntrue and loyal wife to me, be a demon.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nI was nervous from loss of sleep, and the proximity of the beautiful\r\nwoman affected me like a fever. I no longer recall what I said, but I\r\nremember that I kissed her feet, and finally raised her foot and put my\r\nneck under it. She withdrew it quickly, and rose almost angrily.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cIf you love me, Severin,\xe2\x80\x9d she said quickly, and her voice sounded\r\nsharp and commanding, \xe2\x80\x9cnever speak to me of those things again.\r\nUnderstand, never! Otherwise I might really\xe2\x80\x94\xe2\x80\x9d She smiled and sat down\r\nagain.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI am entirely serious,\xe2\x80\x9d I exclaimed, half-raving. \xe2\x80\x9cI adore you so\r\ninfinitely that I am willing to suffer anything from you, for the sake\r\nof spending my whole life near you.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cSeverin, once more I warn you.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYour warning is vain. Do with me what you will, as long as you don\xe2\x80\x99t\r\ndrive me away.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cSeverin,\xe2\x80\x9d replied Wanda, \xe2\x80\x9cI am a frivolous young woman; it is\r\ndangerous for you to put yourself so completely in my power. You will\r\nend by actually becoming a plaything to me. Who will give warrant that\r\nI shall not abuse your insane desire?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYour own nobility of character.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cPower makes people over-bearing.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cBe it,\xe2\x80\x9d I cried, \xe2\x80\x9ctread me underfoot.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nWanda threw her arms around my neck, looked into my eyes, and shook her\r\nhead.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI am afraid I can\xe2\x80\x99t, but I will try, for your sake, for I love you\r\nSeverin, as I have loved no other man.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n*       *       *       *       *\r\n\r\nTo-day she suddenly took her hat and shawl, and I had to go shopping\r\nwith her. She looked at whips, long whips with a short handle, the kind\r\nthat are used on dogs.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cAre these satisfactory?\xe2\x80\x9d said the shopkeeper.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cNo, they are much too small,\xe2\x80\x9d replied Wanda, with a side-glance at me.\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI need a large\xe2\x80\x94\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cFor a bull-dog, I suppose?\xe2\x80\x9d opined the merchant.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYes,\xe2\x80\x9d she exclaimed, \xe2\x80\x9cof the kind that are used in Russia for\r\nintractable slaves.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nShe looked further and finally selected a whip, at whose sight I felt a\r\nstrange creeping sensation.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cNow good-by, Severin,\xe2\x80\x9d she said. \xe2\x80\x9cI have some other purchases to make,\r\nbut you can\xe2\x80\x99t go along.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nI left her and took a walk. On the way back I saw Wanda coming out at a\r\nfurrier\xe2\x80\x99s. She beckoned me.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cConsider it well,\xe2\x80\x9d she began in good spirits, \xe2\x80\x9cI have never made a\r\nsecret of how deeply your serious, dreamy character has fascinated me.\r\nThe idea of seeing this serious man wholly in my power, actually lying\r\nenraptured at my feet, of course, stimulates me\xe2\x80\x94but will this\r\nattraction last? Woman loves a man; she maltreats a slave, and ends by\r\nkicking him aside.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cVery well then, kick me aside,\xe2\x80\x9d I replied, \xe2\x80\x9cwhen you are tired of me.\r\nI want to be your slave.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cDangerous forces lie within me,\xe2\x80\x9d said Wanda, after we had gone a few\r\nsteps further. \xe2\x80\x9cYou awaken them, and not to your advantage. You know\r\nhow to paint pleasure, cruelty, arrogance in glowing colors. What would\r\nyou say should I try my hand at them, and make you the first object of\r\nmy experiments. I would be like Dionysius who had the inventor of the\r\niron ox roasted within it in order to see whether his wails and groans\r\nreally resembled the bellowing of an ox.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cPerhaps I am a female Dionysius?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cBe it,\xe2\x80\x9d I exclaimed, \xe2\x80\x9cand my dreams will be fulfilled. I am yours for\r\ngood or evil, choose. The destiny that lies concealed within my breast\r\ndrives me on\xe2\x80\x94demoniacally\xe2\x80\x94relentlessly.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cMy Beloved,\r\n\r\nI do not care to see you to-day or to-morrow, and not until evening the\r\nday after tomorrow, and then _as my slave_.\r\n\r\nYour mistress\r\n\r\nWanda.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cAs my slave\xe2\x80\x9d was underlined. I read the note which I received early in\r\nthe morning a second time. Then I had a donkey saddled, an animal\r\nsymbolic of learned professors, and rode into the mountains. I wanted\r\nto numb my desire, my yearning, with the magnificent scenery of the\r\nCarpathians. I am back, tired, hungry, thirsty, and more in love than\r\never. I quickly change my clothes, and a few moments later knock at her\r\ndoor.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cCome in!\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nI enter. She is standing in the center of the room, dressed in a gown\r\nof white satin which floods down her body like light. Over it she wears\r\na scarlet _kazabaika_, richly edged with ermine. Upon her powdered,\r\nsnowy hair is a little diadem of diamonds. She stands with her arms\r\nfolded across her breast, and with her brows contracted.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWanda!\xe2\x80\x9d I run toward her, and am about to throw my arm about her to\r\nkiss her. She retreats a step, measuring me from top to bottom.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cSlave!\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cMistress!\xe2\x80\x9d I kneel down, and kiss the hem of her garment.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThat is as it should be.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cOh, how beautiful you are.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cDo I please you?\xe2\x80\x9d She stepped before the mirror, and looked at herself\r\nwith proud satisfaction.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI shall become mad!\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nHer lower lip twitched derisively, and she looked at me mockingly from\r\nbehind half-closed lids.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cGive me the whip.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nI looked about the room.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cNo,\xe2\x80\x9d she exclaimed, \xe2\x80\x9cstay as you are, kneeling.\xe2\x80\x9d She went over to the\r\nfire-place, took the whip from the mantle-piece, and, watching me with\r\na smile, let it hiss through the air; then she slowly rolled up the\r\nsleeve of her fur-jacket.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cMarvellous woman!\xe2\x80\x9d I exclaimed.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cSilence, slave!\xe2\x80\x9d She suddenly scowled, looked savage, and struck me\r\nwith the whip. A moment later she threw her arm tenderly about me, and\r\npityingly bent down to me. \xe2\x80\x9cDid I hurt you?\xe2\x80\x9d she asked, half-shyly,\r\nhalf-timidly.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cNo,\xe2\x80\x9d I replied, \xe2\x80\x9cand even if you had, pains that come through you are\r\na joy. Strike again, if it gives you pleasure.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cBut it doesn\xe2\x80\x99t give me pleasure.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nAgain I was seized with that strange intoxication.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhip me,\xe2\x80\x9d I begged, \xe2\x80\x9cwhip me without mercy.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nWanda swung the whip, and hit me twice. \xe2\x80\x9cAre you satisfied now?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cNo.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cSeriously, no?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhip me, I beg you, it is a joy to me.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYes, because you know very well that it isn\xe2\x80\x99t serious,\xe2\x80\x9d she replied,\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cbecause I haven\xe2\x80\x99t the heart to hurt you. This brutal game goes against\r\nmy grain. Were I really the woman who beats her slaves you would be\r\nhorrified.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cNo, Wanda,\xe2\x80\x9d I replied, \xe2\x80\x9cI love you more than myself; I am devoted to\r\nyou for death and life. In all seriousness, you can do with me whatever\r\nyou will, whatever your caprice suggests.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cSeverin!\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cTread me underfoot!\xe2\x80\x9d I exclaimed, and flung myself face to the floor\r\nbefore her.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI hate all this play-acting,\xe2\x80\x9d said Wanda impatiently.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWell, then maltreat me seriously.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nAn uncanny pause.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cSeverin, I warn you for the last time,\xe2\x80\x9d began Wanda.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cIf you love me, be cruel towards me,\xe2\x80\x9d I pleaded with upraised eyes.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cIf I love you,\xe2\x80\x9d repeated Wanda. \xe2\x80\x9cVery well!\xe2\x80\x9d She stepped back and\r\nlooked at me with a sombre smile. _\xe2\x80\x9cBe then my slave, and know what it\r\nmeans to be delivered into the hands of a woman.\xe2\x80\x9d_ And at the same\r\nmoment she gave me a kick.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cHow do you like that, slave?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nThen she flourished the whip.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cGet up!\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nI was about to rise.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cNot that way,\xe2\x80\x9d she commanded, \xe2\x80\x9con your knees.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nI obeyed, and she began to apply the lash.\r\n\r\nThe blows fell rapidly and powerfully on my back and arms. Each one cut\r\ninto my flesh and burned there, but the pains enraptured me. They came\r\nfrom her whom I adored, and for whom I was ready at any hour to lay\r\ndown my life.\r\n\r\nShe stopped. \xe2\x80\x9cI am beginning to enjoy it,\xe2\x80\x9d she said, \xe2\x80\x9cbut enough for\r\nto-day. I am beginning to feel a demonic curiosity to see how far your\r\nstrength goes. I take a cruel joy in seeing you tremble and writhe\r\nbeneath my whip, and in hearing your groans and wails; I want to go on\r\nwhipping without pity until you beg for mercy, until you lose your\r\nsenses. You have awakened dangerous elements in my being. But now get\r\nup.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nI seized her hand to press it to my lips.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhat impudence.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nShe shoved me away with her foot.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cOut of my sight, slave!\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n*       *       *       *       *\r\n\r\nAfter having spent a feverish night filled with confused dreams, I\r\nawoke. Dawn was just beginning to break.\r\n\r\nHow much of what was hovering in my memory was true; what had I\r\nactually experienced and what had I dreamed? That I had been whipped\r\nwas certain. I can still feel each blow, and count the burning red\r\nstripes on my body. And _she_ whipped me. Now I know everything.\r\n\r\nMy dream has become truth. How does it make me feel? Am I disappointed\r\nin the realization of my dream?\r\n\r\nNo, I am merely somewhat tired, but her cruelty has enraptured me. Oh,\r\nhow I love her, adore her! All this cannot express in the remotest way\r\nmy feeling for her, my complete devotion to her. What happiness to be\r\nher slave!\r\n\r\n*       *       *       *       *\r\n\r\nShe calls to me from her balcony. I hurry upstairs. She is standing on\r\nthe threshold, holding out her hand in friendly fashion. \xe2\x80\x9cI am ashamed\r\nof myself,\xe2\x80\x9d she says, while I embrace her, and she hides her head\r\nagainst my breast.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhy?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cPlease try to forget the ugly scene of yesterday,\xe2\x80\x9d she said with\r\nquivering voice, \xe2\x80\x9cI have fulfilled your mad wish, now let us be\r\nreasonable and happy and love each other, and in a year I will be your\r\nwife.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cMy mistress,\xe2\x80\x9d I exclaimed, \xe2\x80\x9cand I your slave!\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cNot another word of slavery, cruelty, or the whip,\xe2\x80\x9d interrupted Wanda.\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI shall not grant you any of those favors, none except wearing my\r\nfur-jacket; come and help me into it.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n*       *       *       *       *\r\n\r\nThe little bronze clock on which stood a cupid who had just shot his\r\nbolt struck midnight.\r\n\r\nI rose, and wanted to leave.\r\n\r\nWanda said nothing, but embraced me and drew me back on the ottoman.\r\nShe began to kiss me anew, and this silent language was so\r\ncomprehensible, so convincing\xe2\x80\x94\r\n\r\nAnd it told me more than I dared to understand.\r\n\r\nA languid abandonment pervaded Wanda\xe2\x80\x99s entire being. What a voluptuous\r\nsoftness there was in the gloaming of her half-closed eyes, in the red\r\nflood of her hair which shimmered faintly under the white powder, in\r\nthe red and white satin which crackled about her with every movement,\r\nin the swelling ermine of the _kazabaika_ in which she carelessly\r\nnestled.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cPlease,\xe2\x80\x9d I stammered, \xe2\x80\x9cbut you will be angry with me.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cDo with me what you will,\xe2\x80\x9d she whispered.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWell, then whip me, or I shall go mad.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cHaven\xe2\x80\x99t I forbidden you,\xe2\x80\x9d said Wanda sternly, \xe2\x80\x9cbut you are\r\nincorrigible.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cOh, I am so terribly in love.\xe2\x80\x9d I had sunken on my knees, and was\r\nburying my glowing face in her lap.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI really believe,\xe2\x80\x9d said Wanda thoughtfully, \xe2\x80\x9cthat your madness is\r\nnothing but a demonic, unsatisfied sensuality. _Our unnatural way of\r\nlife must generate such illnesses._ Were you less virtuous, you would\r\nbe completely sane.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWell then, make me sane,\xe2\x80\x9d I murmured. My hands were running through\r\nher hair and playing tremblingly with the gleaming fur, which rose and\r\nfell like a moonlit wave upon her heaving bosom, and drove all my\r\nsenses into confusion.\r\n\r\nAnd I kissed her. No, she kissed me savagely, pitilessly, as if she\r\nwanted to slay me with her kisses. I was as in a delirium, and had long\r\nsince lost my reason, but now I, too, was breathless. I sought to free\r\nmyself.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhat is the matter?\xe2\x80\x9d asked Wanda.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI am suffering agonies.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYou are suffering\xe2\x80\x94\xe2\x80\x9d she broke out into a loud amused laughter.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYou laugh!\xe2\x80\x9d I moaned, \xe2\x80\x9chave you no idea\xe2\x80\x94\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nShe was serious all of a sudden. She raised my head in her hands, and\r\nwith a violent gesture drew me to her breast.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWanda,\xe2\x80\x9d I stammered.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cOf course, you enjoy suffering,\xe2\x80\x9d she said, and laughed again, \xe2\x80\x9cbut\r\nwait, I\xe2\x80\x99ll bring you to your senses.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cNo, I will no longer ask,\xe2\x80\x9d I exclaimed, \xe2\x80\x9cwhether you want to belong to\r\nme for always or for only a brief moment of intoxication. I want to\r\ndrain my happiness to the full. You are mine now, and I would rather\r\nlose you than never to have had you.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cNow you are sensible,\xe2\x80\x9d she said. She kissed me again with her\r\nmurderous lips. I tore the ermine apart and the covering of lace and\r\nher naked breast surged against mine.\r\n\r\nThen my senses left me\xe2\x80\x94\r\n\r\nThe first thing I remember is the moment when I saw blood dripping from\r\nmy hand, and she asked apathetically: \xe2\x80\x9cDid you scratch me?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cNo, I believe, I have bitten you.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n*       *       *       *       *\r\n\r\nIt is strange how every relation in life assumes a different face as\r\nsoon as a new person enters.\r\n\r\nWe spent marvellous days together; we visited the mountains and lakes,\r\nwe read together, and I completed Wanda\xe2\x80\x99s portrait. And how we loved\r\none another, how beautiful her smiling face was!\r\n\r\nThen a friend of hers arrived, a divorced woman somewhat older, more\r\nexperienced, and less scrupulous than Wanda. Her influence is already\r\nmaking itself felt in every direction.\r\n\r\nWanda wrinkles her brows, and displays a certain impatience with me.\r\n\r\nHas she ceased loving me?\r\n\r\n*       *       *       *       *\r\n\r\nFor almost a fortnight this unbearable restraint has lain upon us. Her\r\nfriend lives with her, and we are never alone. A circle of men\r\nsurrounds the young women. With my seriousness and melancholy I am\r\nplaying an absurd role as lover. Wanda treats me like a stranger.\r\n\r\nTo-day, while out walking, she staid behind with me. I saw that this\r\nwas done intentionally, and I rejoiced. But what did she tell me?\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cMy friend doesn\xe2\x80\x99t understand how I can love you. She doesn\xe2\x80\x99t think you\r\neither handsome or particularly attractive otherwise. She is telling me\r\nfrom morning till night about the glamour of the frivolous life in the\r\ncapital, hinting at the advantages to which I could lay claim, the\r\nlarge parties which I would find there, and the distinguished and\r\nhandsome admirers which I would attract. But of what use is all this,\r\nsince it happens that I love you.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nFor a moment I lost my breath, then I said: \xe2\x80\x9cI have no wish to stand in\r\nthe way of your happiness, Wanda. Do not consider me.\xe2\x80\x9d Then I raised my\r\nhat, and let her go ahead. She looked at me surprised, but did not\r\nanswer a syllable.\r\n\r\nWhen by chance I happened to be close to her on the way back, she\r\nsecretly pressed my hand. Her glance was so radiant, so full of\r\npromised happiness, that in a moment all the torments of these days\r\nwere forgotten and all their wounds healed.\r\n\r\nI now am aware again of how much I love her.\r\n\r\n*       *       *       *       *\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cMy friend has complained about you,\xe2\x80\x9d said Wanda to-day.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cPerhaps she feels that I despise her.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cBut why do you despise her, you foolish young man?\xe2\x80\x9d exclaimed Wanda,\r\npulling my ears with both hands.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cBecause she is a hypocrite,\xe2\x80\x9d I said. \xe2\x80\x9cI respect only a woman who is\r\nactually virtuous, or who openly lives for pleasure\xe2\x80\x99s sake.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cLike me, for instance,\xe2\x80\x9d replied Wanda jestingly, \xe2\x80\x9cbut you see, child,\r\na woman can only do that in the rarest cases. She can neither be as\r\ngaily sensual, nor as spiritually free as man; her state is always a\r\nmixture of the sensual and spiritual. Her heart desires to enchain man\r\npermanently, while she herself is ever subject to the desire for\r\nchange. The result is a conflict, and thus usually against her wishes\r\nlies and deception enter into her actions and personality and corrupt\r\nher character.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cCertainly that is true,\xe2\x80\x9d I said. \xe2\x80\x9cThe transcendental character with\r\nwhich woman wants to stamp love leads her to deception.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cBut the world likewise demands it,\xe2\x80\x9d Wanda interrupted. \xe2\x80\x9cLook at this\r\nwoman. She has a husband and a lover in Lemberg and has found a new\r\nadmirer here. She deceives all three and yet is honored by all and\r\nrespected by the world.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI don\xe2\x80\x99t care,\xe2\x80\x9d I exclaimed, \xe2\x80\x9cbut she is to leave you alone; she treats\r\nyou like an article of commerce.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhy not?\xe2\x80\x9d the beautiful woman interrupted vivaciously. \xe2\x80\x9cEvery woman\r\nhas the instinct or desire to draw advantage out of her attractions,\r\nand much is to be said for giving one\xe2\x80\x99s self without love or pleasure\r\nbecause if you do it in cold blood, you can reap profit to best\r\nadvantage.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWanda, what are you saying?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhy not?\xe2\x80\x9d she said, \xe2\x80\x9cand take note of what I am about to say to you.\r\n_Never feel secure with the woman you love,_ for there are more dangers\r\nin woman\xe2\x80\x99s nature than you imagine. Women are neither as _good_ as\r\ntheir admirers and defenders maintain, nor as _bad_ as their enemies\r\nmake them out to be. _Woman\xe2\x80\x99s character is characterlessness._ The best\r\nwoman will momentarily go down into the mire, and the worst\r\nunexpectedly rises to deeds of greatness and goodness and puts to shame\r\nthose that despise her. No woman is so good or so bad, but that at any\r\nmoment she is capable of the most diabolical as well as of the most\r\ndivine, of the filthiest as well as of the purest, thoughts, emotions,\r\nand actions. In spite of all the advances of civilization, woman has\r\nremained as she came out of the hand of nature. She has the nature of a\r\nsavage, who is faithful or faithless, magnanimous or cruel, according\r\nto the impulse that dominates at the moment. Throughout history it has\r\nalways been a serious deep culture which has produced moral character.\r\nMan even when he is selfish or evil always follows _principles,_ woman\r\nnever follows anything but _impulses._ Don\xe2\x80\x99t ever forget that, and\r\nnever feel secure with the woman you love.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n*       *       *       *       *\r\n\r\nHer friend has left. At last an evening alone with her again. It seems\r\nas if Wanda had saved up all the love, which had been kept from her,\r\nfor this superlative evening; never had she been so kind, so near, so\r\nfull of tenderness.\r\n\r\nWhat happiness to cling to her lips, and to die away in her arms! In a\r\nstate of relaxation and wholly mine, her head rests against my breast,\r\nand with drunken rapture our eyes seek each other.\r\n\r\nI cannot yet believe, comprehend, that this woman is mine, wholly mine.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cShe is right on one point,\xe2\x80\x9d Wanda began, without moving, without\r\nopening her eyes, as if she were asleep.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWho?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nShe remained silent.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYour friend?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nShe nodded. \xe2\x80\x9cYes, she is right, you are not a man, you are a dreamer, a\r\ncharming cavalier, and you certainly would be a priceless slave, but I\r\ncannot imagine you as husband.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nI was frightened.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhat is the matter? You are trembling?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI tremble at the thought of how easily I might lose you,\xe2\x80\x9d I replied.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cAre you made less happy now, because of this?\xe2\x80\x9d she replied. \xe2\x80\x9cDoes it\r\nrob you of any of your joys, that I have belonged to another before I\r\ndid to you, that others after you will possess me, and would you enjoy\r\nless if another were made happy simultaneously with you?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWanda!\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYou see,\xe2\x80\x9d she continued, \xe2\x80\x9cthat would be a way out. You won\xe2\x80\x99t ever lose\r\nme then. I care deeply for you and intellectually we are harmonious,\r\nand I should like to live with you always, if in addition to you I\r\nmight have\xe2\x80\x94\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhat an idea,\xe2\x80\x9d I cried. \xe2\x80\x9cYou fill me with a sort of horror.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cDo you love me any the less?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cOn the contrary.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nWanda had raised herself on her left arm. \xe2\x80\x9cI believe,\xe2\x80\x9d she said, \xe2\x80\x9cthat\r\nto hold a man permanently, it is vitally important not to be faithful\r\nto him. What honest woman has ever been as devotedly loved as a\r\nhetaira?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThere is a painful stimulus in the unfaithfulness of a beloved woman.\r\nIt is the highest kind of ecstacy.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cFor you, too?\xe2\x80\x9d Wanda asked quickly.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cFor me, too.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cAnd if I should give you that pleasure,\xe2\x80\x9d Wanda exclaimed mockingly.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI shall suffer terrible agonies, but I shall adore you the more,\xe2\x80\x9d I\r\nreplied. \xe2\x80\x9cBut you would never deceive me, you would have the daemonic\r\ngreatness of saying to me: I shall love no one but you, but I shall\r\nmake happy whoever pleases me.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nWanda shook her head. \xe2\x80\x9cI don\xe2\x80\x99t like deception, I am honest, but what\r\nman exists who can support the burden of truth. Were I say to you: this\r\nserene, sensual life, this paganism is my ideal, would you be strong\r\nenough to bear it?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cCertainly. I could endure anything so as not to lose you. I feel how\r\nlittle I really mean to you.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cBut Severin\xe2\x80\x94\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cBut it is so,\xe2\x80\x9d said I, \xe2\x80\x9cand just for that reason\xe2\x80\x94\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cFor that reason you would\xe2\x80\x94\xe2\x80\x9d she smiled roguishly\xe2\x80\x94\xe2\x80\x9chave I guessed it?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cBe your slave!\xe2\x80\x9d I exclaimed. \xe2\x80\x9cBe your unrestricted property, without a\r\nwill of my own, of which you could dispose as you wished, and which\r\nwould therefore never be a burden to you. While you drink life at its\r\nfullness, while surrounded by luxury, you enjoy the serene happiness\r\nand Olympian love, I want to be your servant, put on and take off your\r\nshoes.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYou really aren\xe2\x80\x99t so far from wrong,\xe2\x80\x9d replied Wanda, \xe2\x80\x9cfor only as my\r\nslave could you endure my loving others. Furthermore the freedom of\r\nenjoyment of the ancient world is unthinkable without slavery. It must\r\ngive one a feeling of like unto a god to see a man kneel before one and\r\ntremble. I want a slave, do you hear, Severin?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cAm I not your slave?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThen listen to me,\xe2\x80\x9d said Wanda excitedly, seizing my hand. \xe2\x80\x9cI want to\r\nbe yours, as long as I love you.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cA month?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cPerhaps, even two.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cAnd then?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThen you become my slave.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cAnd you?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI? Why do you ask? I am a goddess and sometimes I descend from my\r\nOlympian heights to you, softly, very softly, and secretly.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cBut what does all this mean,\xe2\x80\x9d said Wanda, resting her head in both\r\nhands with her gaze lost in the distance, \xe2\x80\x9ca golden fancy which never\r\ncan become true.\xe2\x80\x9d An uncanny brooding melancholy seemed shed over her\r\nentire being; I have never seen her like that.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhy unachievable?\xe2\x80\x9d I began.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cBecause slavery doesn\xe2\x80\x99t exist any longer.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThen we will go to a country where it still exists, to the Orient, to\r\nTurkey,\xe2\x80\x9d I said eagerly.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYou would\xe2\x80\x94Severin\xe2\x80\x94in all seriousness,\xe2\x80\x9d Wanda replied. Her eyes burned.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYes, in all seriousness, I want to be your slave,\xe2\x80\x9d I continued. \xe2\x80\x9cI\r\nwant your power over me to be sanctified by law; I want my life to be\r\nin your hands, I want nothing that could protect or save me from you.\r\nOh, what a voluptuous joy when once I feel myself entirely dependent\r\nupon your absolute will, your whim, at your beck and call. And then\r\nwhat happiness, when at some time you deign to be gracious, and the\r\nslave may kiss the lips which mean life and death to him.\xe2\x80\x9d I knelt\r\ndown, and leaned my burning forehead against her knee.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYou are talking as in a fever,\xe2\x80\x9d said Wanda agitatedly, \xe2\x80\x9cand you really\r\nlove me so endlessly.\xe2\x80\x9d She held me to her breast, and covered me with\r\nkisses.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYou really want it?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI swear to you now by God and my honor, that I shall be your slave,\r\nwherever and whenever you wish it, as soon as you command,\xe2\x80\x9d I\r\nexclaimed, hardly master of myself.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cAnd if I take you at your word?\xe2\x80\x9d said Wanda.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cPlease do!\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cAll this appeals to me,\xe2\x80\x9d she said then. \xe2\x80\x9cIt is different from anything\r\nelse\xe2\x80\x94to know that a man who worships me, and whom I love with all my\r\nheart, is so wholly mine, dependent on my will and caprice, my\r\npossession and slave, while I\xe2\x80\x94\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nShe looked strangely at me.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cIf I should become frightfully frivolous you are to blame,\xe2\x80\x9d she\r\ncontinued. \xe2\x80\x9cIt almost seems as if you were afraid of me already, but\r\nyou have sworn.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cAnd I shall keep my oath.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI shall see to that,\xe2\x80\x9d she replied. \xe2\x80\x9cI am beginning to enjoy it, and,\r\nheaven help me, we won\xe2\x80\x99t stick to fancies now. You shall become my\r\nslave, and I\xe2\x80\x94I shall try to be _Venus in Furs_.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n*       *       *       *       *\r\n\r\nI thought that at last I knew this woman, understood her, and now I see\r\nI have to begin at the very beginning again. Only a little while ago\r\nher reaction to my dreams was violently hostile, and now she tries to\r\ncarry them into execution with the soberest seriousness.\r\n\r\nShe has drawn up a contract according to which I give my word of honor\r\nand agree under oath to be her slave, as long as she wishes.\r\n\r\nWith her arm around my neck she reads this, unprecedented, incredible\r\ndocument to me. The end of each sentence she punctuates with a kiss.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cBut all the obligations in the contract are on my side,\xe2\x80\x9d I said,\r\nteasing her.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cOf course,\xe2\x80\x9d she replied with great seriousness, \xe2\x80\x9cyou cease to be my\r\nlover, and consequently I am released from all duties and obligations\r\ntowards you. You will have to look upon my favors as pure benevolence.\r\nYou no longer have any rights, and no longer can lay claim to any.\r\nThere can be no limit to my power over you. Remember, that you won\xe2\x80\x99t be\r\nmuch better than a dog, or some inanimate object. You will be mine, my\r\nplaything, which I can break to pieces, whenever I want an hour\xe2\x80\x99s\r\namusement. You are nothing, I am everything. Do you understand?\xe2\x80\x9d She\r\nlaughed and kissed me again, and yet a sort of cold shiver ran through\r\nme.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWon\xe2\x80\x99t you allow me a few conditions\xe2\x80\x94\xe2\x80\x9d I began.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cConditions?\xe2\x80\x9d She contracted her forehead. \xe2\x80\x9cAh! You are afraid already,\r\nor perhaps you regret, but it is too late now. You have sworn, I have\r\nyour word of honor. But let me hear them.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cFirst of all I should like to have it included in our contract, that\r\nyou will never completely leave me, and then that you will never give\r\nme over to the mercies of any of your admirers\xe2\x80\x94\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cBut Severin,\xe2\x80\x9d exclaimed Wanda with her voice full of emotion and with\r\ntears in her eyes, \xe2\x80\x9chow can you imagine that I\xe2\x80\x94and you, a man who loves\r\nme so absolutely, who puts himself so entirely in my power\xe2\x80\x94\xe2\x80\x9d She\r\nhalted.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cNo, no!\xe2\x80\x9d I said, covering her hands with kisses. \xe2\x80\x9cI don\xe2\x80\x99t fear\r\nanything from you that might dishonor me. Forgive me the ugly thought.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nWanda smiled happily, leaned her cheek against mine, and seemed to\r\nreflect.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYou have forgotten something,\xe2\x80\x9d she whispered coquettishly, \xe2\x80\x9cthe most\r\nimportant thing!\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cA condition?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYes, that I must always wear my furs,\xe2\x80\x9d exclaimed Wanda. \xe2\x80\x9cBut I promise\r\nyou I\xe2\x80\x99ll do that anyhow because they give me a despotic feeling. And I\r\nshall be very cruel to you, do you understand?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cShall I sign the contract?\xe2\x80\x9d I asked.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cNot yet,\xe2\x80\x9d said Wanda. \xe2\x80\x9cI shall first add your conditions, and the\r\nactual signing won\xe2\x80\x99t occur until the proper time and place.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cIn Constantinople?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cNo. I have thought things over. What special value would there be in\r\nowning a slave where everyone owns slaves. What I want is to _have a\r\nslave, I alone,_ here in our civilized sober, Philistine world, and a\r\nslave who submits helplessly to my power solely on account of my beauty\r\nand personality, not because of law, of property rights, or\r\ncompulsions. This attracts me. But at any rate we will go to a country\r\nwhere we are not known and where you can appear before the world as my\r\nservant without embarrassment. Perhaps to Italy, to Rome or Naples.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n*       *       *       *       *\r\n\r\nWe were sitting on Wanda\xe2\x80\x99s ottoman. She wore her ermine jacket, her\r\nhair was loose and fell like a lion\xe2\x80\x99s mane down her back. She clung to\r\nmy lips, drawing my soul from my body. My head whirled, my blood began\r\nto seethe, my heart beat violently against hers.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI want to be absolutely in your power, Wanda,\xe2\x80\x9d I exclaimed suddenly,\r\nseized by that frenzy of passion when I can scarcely think clearly or\r\ndecide freely. \xe2\x80\x9cI want to put myself absolutely at your mercy for good\r\nor evil without any condition, without any limit to your power.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nWhile saying this I had slipped from the ottoman, and lay at her feet\r\nlooking up at her with drunken eyes.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cHow beautiful you now are,\xe2\x80\x9d she exclaimed, \xe2\x80\x9cyour eyes half-broken in\r\necstacy fill me with joy, carry me away. How wonderful your look would\r\nbe if you were being beaten to death, in the extreme agony. You have\r\nthe eye of a martyr.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n*       *       *       *       *\r\n\r\nSometimes, nevertheless, I have an uneasy feeling about placing myself\r\nso absolutely, so unconditionally into a woman\xe2\x80\x99s hands. Suppose she did\r\nabuse my passion, her power?\r\n\r\nWell, then I would experience what has occupied my imagination since my\r\nchildhood, what has always given me the feeling of seductive terror. A\r\nfoolish apprehension! It will be a wanton game she will play with me,\r\nnothing more. She loves me, and she is good, a noble personality,\r\nincapable of a breach of faith. But it lies in her hands \xe2\x80\x94_if she wants\r\nto she can._ What a temptation in this doubt, this fear!\r\n\r\nNow I understand Manon l\xe2\x80\x99Escault and the poor chevalier, who, even in\r\nthe pillory, while she was another man\xe2\x80\x99s mistress, still adored her.\r\n\r\nLove knows no virtue, no profit; it loves and forgives and suffers\r\neverything, because it must. It is not our judgment that leads us; it\r\nis neither the advantages nor the faults which we discover, that make\r\nus abandon ourselves, or that repel us.\r\n\r\nIt is a sweet, soft, enigmatic power that drives us on. We cease to\r\nthink, to feel, to will; we let ourselves be carried away by it, and\r\nask not whither?\r\n\r\n*       *       *       *       *\r\n\r\nA Russian prince made his first appearance today on the promenade. He\r\naroused general interest on account of his athletic figure, magnificent\r\nface, and splendid bearing. The women particularly gaped at him as\r\nthough he were a wild animal, but he went his way gloomily without\r\npaying attention to any one. He was accompanied by two servants, one a\r\nnegro, completely dressed in red satin, and the other a Circassian in\r\nhis full gleaming uniform. Suddenly he saw Wanda, and fixed his cold\r\npiercing look upon her; he even turned his head after her, and when she\r\nhad passed, he stood still and followed her with his eyes.\r\n\r\nAnd she\xe2\x80\x94she veritably devoured him with her radiant green eyes\xe2\x80\x94and did\r\neverything possible to meet him again.\r\n\r\nThe cunning coquetry with which she walked, moved, and looked at him,\r\nalmost stifled me. On the way home I remarked about it. She knit her\r\nbrows.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhat do you want,\xe2\x80\x9d she said, \xe2\x80\x9cthe prince is a man whom I might like,\r\nwho even dazzles me, and I am free. I can do what I please\xe2\x80\x94\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cDon\xe2\x80\x99t you love me any longer\xe2\x80\x94\xe2\x80\x9d I stammered, frightened.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI love only you,\xe2\x80\x9d she replied, \xe2\x80\x9cbut I shall have the prince pay court\r\nto me.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWanda!\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cAren\xe2\x80\x99t you my slave?\xe2\x80\x9d she said calmly. \xe2\x80\x9cAm I not Venus, the cruel\r\nnorthern Venus in Furs?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nI was silent. I felt literally crushed by her words; her cold look\r\nentered my heart like a dagger.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYou will find out immediately the prince\xe2\x80\x99s name, residence, and\r\ncircumstances,\xe2\x80\x9d she continued. \xe2\x80\x9cDo you understand?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cBut\xe2\x80\x94\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cNo argument, obey!\xe2\x80\x9d exclaimed Wanda, more sternly than I would have\r\nthought possible for her, \xe2\x80\x9cand don\xe2\x80\x99t dare to enter my sight until you\r\ncan answer my questions.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nIt was not till afternoon that I could obtain the desired information\r\nfor Wanda. She let me stand before her like a servant, while she leaned\r\nback in her arm-chair and listened to me, smiling. Then she nodded; she\r\nseemed to be satisfied.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cBring me my footstool,\xe2\x80\x9d she commanded shortly.\r\n\r\nI obeyed, and after having put it before her and having put her feet on\r\nit, I remained kneeling.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cHow will this end?\xe2\x80\x9d I asked sadly after a short pause.\r\n\r\nShe broke into playful laughter. \xe2\x80\x9cWhy things haven\xe2\x80\x99t even begun yet.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYou are more heartless than I imagined,\xe2\x80\x9d I replied, hurt.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cSeverin,\xe2\x80\x9d Wanda began earnestly. \xe2\x80\x9cI haven\xe2\x80\x99t done anything yet, not the\r\nslightest thing, and you are already calling me heartless. What will\r\nhappen when I begin to carry your dreams to their realization, when I\r\nshall lead a gay, free life and have a circle of admirers about me,\r\nwhen I shall actually fulfil your ideal, tread you underfoot and apply\r\nthe lash?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYou take my dreams too seriously.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cToo seriously? I can\xe2\x80\x99t stop at make-believe, when once I begin,\xe2\x80\x9d she\r\nreplied. \xe2\x80\x9cYou know I hate all play-acting and comedy. You have wished\r\nit. Was it my idea or yours? Did I persuade you or did you inflame my\r\nimagination? I am taking things seriously now.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWanda,\xe2\x80\x9d I replied, caressingly, \xe2\x80\x9clisten quietly to me. We love each\r\nother infinitely, we are very happy, will you sacrifice our entire\r\nfuture to a whim?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cIt is no longer a whim,\xe2\x80\x9d she exclaimed.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhat is it?\xe2\x80\x9d I asked frightened.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cSomething that was probably latent in me,\xe2\x80\x9d she said quietly and\r\nthoughtfully. \xe2\x80\x9cPerhaps it would never have come to light, if you had\r\nnot called it to life, and made it grow. Now that it has become a\r\npowerful impulse, fills my whole being, now that I enjoy it, now that I\r\ncannot and do not want to do otherwise, now you want to back out\xe2\x80\x94\r\nyou\xe2\x80\x94are you a man?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cDear, sweet Wanda!\xe2\x80\x9d I began to caress her, kiss her.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cDon\xe2\x80\x99t\xe2\x80\x94you are not a man\xe2\x80\x94\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cAnd you,\xe2\x80\x9d I flared up.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI am stubborn,\xe2\x80\x9d she said, \xe2\x80\x9cyou know that. I haven\xe2\x80\x99t a strong\r\nimagination, and like you I am weak in execution. But when I make up my\r\nmind to do something, I carry it through, and the more certainly, the\r\nmore opposition I meet. Leave me alone!\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nShe pushed me away, and got up.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWanda!\xe2\x80\x9d I likewise rose, and stood facing her.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cNow you know what I am,\xe2\x80\x9d she continued. \xe2\x80\x9cOnce more I warn you. You\r\nstill have the choice. I am not compelling you to be my slave.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWanda,\xe2\x80\x9d I replied with emotion and tears filling my eyes, \xe2\x80\x9cdon\xe2\x80\x99t you\r\nknow how I love you?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nHer lips quivered contemptuously.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYou are mistaken, you make yourself out worse than you are; you are\r\ngood and noble by nature\xe2\x80\x94\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhat do you know about my nature,\xe2\x80\x9d she interrupted vehemently, \xe2\x80\x9cyou\r\nwill get to know me as I am.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWanda!\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cDecide, will you submit, unconditionally?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cAnd if I say no.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThen\xe2\x80\x94\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nShe stepped close up to me, cold and contemptuous. As she stood before\r\nme now, the arms folded across her breast, with an evil smile about her\r\nlips, she was in fact the despotic woman of my dreams. Her expression\r\nseemed hard, and nothing lay in her eyes that promised kindness or\r\nmercy.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWell\xe2\x80\x94\xe2\x80\x9d she said at last.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYou are angry,\xe2\x80\x9d I cried, \xe2\x80\x9cyou will punish me.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cOh no!\xe2\x80\x9d she replied, \xe2\x80\x9cI shall let you go. You are free. I am not\r\nholding you.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWanda\xe2\x80\x94I, who love you so\xe2\x80\x94\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYes, you, my dear sir, you who adore me,\xe2\x80\x9d she exclaimed\r\ncontemptuously, \xe2\x80\x9cbut who are a coward, a liar, and a breaker of\r\npromises. Leave me instantly\xe2\x80\x94\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWanda I\xe2\x80\x94\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWretch!\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nMy blood rose in my heart. I threw myself down at her feet and began to\r\ncry.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cTears, too!\xe2\x80\x9d She began to laugh. Oh, this laughter was frightful.\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cLeave me\xe2\x80\x94I don\xe2\x80\x99t want to see you again.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cOh my God!\xe2\x80\x9d I cried, beside myself. \xe2\x80\x9cI will do whatever you command,\r\nbe your slave, a mere object with which you can do what you will\xe2\x80\x94only\r\ndon\xe2\x80\x99t send me away\xe2\x80\x94I can\xe2\x80\x99t bear it\xe2\x80\x94I cannot live without you.\xe2\x80\x9d I\r\nembraced her knees, and covered her hand with kisses.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYes, you must be a slave, and feel the lash, for you are not a man,\xe2\x80\x9d\r\nshe said calmly. She said this to me with perfect composure, not\r\nangrily, not even excitedly, and it was what hurt most. \xe2\x80\x9cNow I know\r\nyou, your dog-like nature, that adores where it is kicked, and the\r\nmore, the more it is maltreated. Now I know you, and now you shall come\r\nto know me.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nShe walked up and down with long strides, while I remained crushed on\r\nmy knees; my head was hanging supine, tears flowed from my eyes.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cCome here,\xe2\x80\x9d Wanda commanded harshly, sitting down on the ottoman. I\r\nobeyed her command, and sat down beside her. She looked at me sombrely,\r\nand then a light suddenly seemed to illuminate the interior of her eye.\r\nSmiling, she drew me toward her breast, and began to kiss the tears out\r\nof my eyes.\r\n\r\n*       *       *       *       *\r\n\r\nThe odd part of my situation is that I am like the bear in Lily\xe2\x80\x99s park.\r\nI can escape and don\xe2\x80\x99t want to; I am ready to endure everything as soon\r\nas she threatens to set me free.\r\n\r\n*       *       *       *       *\r\n\r\nIf only she would use the whip again. There is something uncanny in the\r\nkindness with which she treats me. I seem like a little captive mouse\r\nwith which a beautiful cat prettily plays. She is ready at any moment\r\nto tear it to pieces, and my heart of a mouse threatens to burst.\r\n\r\nWhat are her intentions? What does she purpose to do with me?\r\n\r\n*       *       *       *       *\r\n\r\nIt seems she has completely forgotten the contract, my slavehood. Or\r\nwas it actually only stubbornness? And she gave up her whole plan as\r\nsoon as I no longer opposed her and submitted to her imperial whim?\r\n\r\nHow kind she is to me, how tender, how loving! We are spending\r\nmarvellously happy days.\r\n\r\nTo-day she had me read to her the scene between Faust and\r\nMephistopheles, in which the latter appears as a wandering scholar. Her\r\nglance hung on me with strange pleasure.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI don\xe2\x80\x99t understand,\xe2\x80\x9d she said when I had finished, \xe2\x80\x9chow a man who can\r\nread such great and beautiful thoughts with such expression, and\r\ninterpret them so clearly, concisely, and intelligently, can at the\r\nsame time be such a visionary and supersensual ninny as you are.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWere you pleased,\xe2\x80\x9d said I, and kissed her forehead.\r\n\r\nShe gently stroked my brow. \xe2\x80\x9cI love you, Severin,\xe2\x80\x9d she whispered. \xe2\x80\x9cI\r\ndon\xe2\x80\x99t believe I could ever love any one more than you. Let us be\r\nsensible, what do you say?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nInstead of replying I folded her in my arms; a deep inward, yet vaguely\r\nsad happiness filled my breast, my eyes grew moist, and a tear fell\r\nupon her hand.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cHow can you cry!\xe2\x80\x9d she exclaimed, \xe2\x80\x9cyou are a child!\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n*       *       *       *       *\r\n\r\nOn a pleasure drive we met the Russian prince in his carriage. He\r\nseemed to be unpleasantly surprised to see me by Wanda\xe2\x80\x99s side, and\r\nlooked as if he wanted to pierce her through and through with his\r\nelectric gray eyes. She, however, did not seem to notice him. I felt at\r\nthat moment like kneeling down before her and kissing her feet. She let\r\nher glance glide over him indifferently as though he were an inanimate\r\nobject, a tree, for instance, and turned to me with her gracious smile.\r\n\r\n*       *       *       *       *\r\n\r\nWhen I said good-night to her to-day she seemed suddenly unaccountably\r\ndistracted and moody. What was occupying her?\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI am sorry you are going,\xe2\x80\x9d she said when I was already standing on the\r\nthreshold.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cIt is entirely in your hands to shorten the hard period of my trial,\r\nto cease tormenting me\xe2\x80\x94\xe2\x80\x9d I pleaded.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cDo you imagine that this compulsion isn\xe2\x80\x99t a torment for me, too,\xe2\x80\x9d\r\nWanda interjected.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThen end it,\xe2\x80\x9d I exclaimed, embracing her, \xe2\x80\x9cbe my wife.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9c_Never, Severin_,\xe2\x80\x9d she said gently, but with great firmness.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhat do you mean?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nI was frightened in my innermost soul.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9c_You are not the man for me._\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nI looked at her, and slowly withdrew my arm which was still about her\r\nwaist; then I left the room, and she\xe2\x80\x94she did not call me back.\r\n\r\n*       *       *       *       *\r\n\r\nA sleepless night; I made countless decisions, only to toss them aside\r\nagain. In the morning I wrote her a letter in which I declared our\r\nrelationship dissolved. My hand trembled when I put on the seal, and I\r\nburned my fingers.\r\n\r\nAs I went upstairs to hand it to the maid, my knees threatened to give\r\nway.\r\n\r\nThe door opened, and Wanda thrust forth her head full of\r\ncurling-papers.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI haven\xe2\x80\x99t had my hair dressed yet,\xe2\x80\x9d she said, smiling. \xe2\x80\x9cWhat have you\r\nthere?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cA letter\xe2\x80\x94\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cFor me?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nI nodded.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cAh, you want to break with me,\xe2\x80\x9d she exclaimed, mockingly.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cDidn\xe2\x80\x99t you tell me yesterday that I wasn\xe2\x80\x99t the man for you?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n_\xe2\x80\x9cI repeat it now!\xe2\x80\x9d_\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cVery well, then.\xe2\x80\x9d My whole body was trembling, my voice failed me, and\r\nI handed her the letter.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cKeep it,\xe2\x80\x9d she said, measuring me coldly. \xe2\x80\x9cYou forget that is no longer\r\na question as to whether you satisfy me as a man; as a _slave_ you will\r\ndoubtless do well enough.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cMadame!\xe2\x80\x9d I exclaimed, aghast.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThat is what you will call me in the future,\xe2\x80\x9d replied Wanda, throwing\r\nback her head with a movement of unutterable contempt. \xe2\x80\x9cPut your\r\naffairs in order within the next twenty-four hours. The day after\r\nto-morrow I shall start for Italy, and you will accompany me as my\r\nservant.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWanda\xe2\x80\x94\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI forbid any sort of familiarity,\xe2\x80\x9d she said, cutting my words short,\r\n\xe2\x80\x9clikewise you are not to come in unless I call or ring for you, and you\r\nare not to speak to me until you are spoken to. From now on your name\r\nis no longer Severin, but _Gregor_.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nI trembled with rage, and yet, unfortunately, I cannot deny it, I also\r\nfelt a strange pleasure and stimulation.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cBut, madame, you know my circumstances,\xe2\x80\x9d I began in my confusion. \xe2\x80\x9cI\r\nam dependent on my father, and I doubt whether he will give me the\r\nlarge sum of money needed for this journey\xe2\x80\x94\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThat means you have no money, Gregor,\xe2\x80\x9d said Wanda, delightedly, \xe2\x80\x9cso\r\nmuch the better, you are then entirely dependent on me, and in fact my\r\nslave.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYou don\xe2\x80\x99t consider,\xe2\x80\x9d I tried to object, \xe2\x80\x9cthat as man of honor it is\r\nimpossible for me\xe2\x80\x94\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI have indeed considered it,\xe2\x80\x9d she replied almost with a tone of\r\ncommand. \xe2\x80\x9cAs a man of honor you must keep your oath and redeem your\r\npromise to follow me as slave whithersoever I demand and to obey\r\nwhatever I command. Now leave me, Gregor!\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nI turned toward the door.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cNot yet\xe2\x80\x94you may first kiss my hand.\xe2\x80\x9d She held it out to me with a\r\ncertain proud indifference, and I the dilettante, the donkey, the\r\nmiserable slave pressed it with intense tenderness against my lips\r\nwhich were dry and hot with excitement.\r\n\r\nThere was another gracious nod of the head.\r\n\r\nThen I was dismissed.\r\n\r\n*       *       *       *       *\r\n\r\nThough it was late in the evening my light was still lit, and a fire\r\nwas burning in the large green stove. There were still many things\r\namong my letters and documents to be put in order. Autumn, as is\r\nusually the case with us, had fallen with all its power.\r\n\r\nSuddenly she knocked at my window with the handle of her whip.\r\n\r\nI opened and saw her standing outside in her ermine-lined jacket and in\r\na high round Cossack cap of ermine of the kind which the great\r\nCatherine favored.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cAre you ready, Gregor?\xe2\x80\x9d she asked darkly.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cNot yet, mistress,\xe2\x80\x9d I replied.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI like that word,\xe2\x80\x9d she said then, \xe2\x80\x9cyou are always to call me mistress,\r\ndo you understand? We leave here to-morrow morning at nine o\xe2\x80\x99clock. As\r\nfar as the district capital you will be my companion and friend, but\r\nfrom the moment that we enter the railway-coach you are my slave, my\r\nservant. Now close the window, and open the door.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nAfter I had done as she had demanded, and after she had entered, she\r\nasked, contracting her brows ironically, \xe2\x80\x9cwell, how do you like me.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWanda, you\xe2\x80\x94\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWho gave you permission?\xe2\x80\x9d She gave me a blow with the whip.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYou are very beautiful, mistress.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nWanda smiled and sat down in the arm-chair. \xe2\x80\x9cKneel down\xe2\x80\x94here beside my\r\nchair.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nI obeyed.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cKiss my hand.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nI seized her small cold hand and kissed it.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cAnd the mouth\xe2\x80\x94\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nIn a surge of passion I threw my arms around the beautiful cruel woman,\r\nand covered her face, arms, and breast with glowing kisses. She\r\nreturned them with equal fervor\xe2\x80\x94the eyelids closed as in a dream. It\r\nwas after midnight when she left.\r\n\r\n*       *       *       *       *\r\n\r\nAt nine o\xe2\x80\x99clock sharp in the morning everything was ready for\r\ndeparture, as she had ordered. We left the little Carpathian\r\nhealth-resort in a comfortable light carriage. The most interesting\r\ndrama of my life had reached a point of development whose denouement it\r\nwas then impossible to foretell.\r\n\r\nSo far everything went well. I sat beside Wanda, and she chatted very\r\ngraciously and intelligently with me, as with a good friend, concerning\r\nItaly, Pisemski\xe2\x80\x99s new novel, and Wagner\xe2\x80\x99s music. She wore a sort of\r\nAmazonesque travelling-dress of black cloth with a short jacket of the\r\nsame material, set with dark fur. It fitted closely and showed her\r\nfigure to best advantage. Over it she wore dark furs. Her hair wound\r\ninto an antique knot, lay beneath a small dark fur-hat from which a\r\nblack veil hung. Wanda was in very good humor; she fed me candies,\r\nplayed with my hair, loosened my neck cloth and made a pretty cockade\r\nof it; she covered my knees with her furs and stealthily pressed the\r\nfingers of my hand. When our Jewish driver persistently went on nodding\r\nto himself, she even gave me a kiss, and her cold lips had the fresh\r\nfrosty fragrance of a young autumnal rose, which blossoms alone amid\r\nbare stalks and yellow leaves and upon whose calyx the first frost has\r\nhung tiny diamonds of ice.\r\n\r\n*       *       *       *       *\r\n\r\nWe are at the district capital. We get out at the railway station.\r\nWanda throws off her furs and places them over my arm, and goes to\r\nsecure the tickets.\r\n\r\nWhen she returns she has completely changed.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cHere is your ticket, Gregor,\xe2\x80\x9d she says in a tone which supercilious\r\nladies use to their servants.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cA third-class ticket,\xe2\x80\x9d I reply with comic horror.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cOf course,\xe2\x80\x9d she continues, \xe2\x80\x9cbut now be careful. You won\xe2\x80\x99t get on until\r\nI am settled in my compartment and don\xe2\x80\x99t need you any longer. At each\r\nstation you will hurry to my car and ask for my orders. Don\xe2\x80\x99t forget.\r\nAnd now give me my furs.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nAfter I had helped her into them, humbly like a slave, she went to find\r\nan empty first-class coupe. I followed. Supporting herself on my\r\nshoulder, she got on and I wrapped her feet in bear-skins and placed\r\nthem on the warming bottle.\r\n\r\nThen she nodded to me, and dismissed me. I slowly ascended a\r\nthird-class carriage, which was filled with abominable tobacco-smoke\r\nthat seemed like the fogs of Acheron at the entrance to Hades. I now\r\nhad the leisure to muse about the riddle of human existence, and about\r\nits greatest riddle of all\xe2\x80\x94_woman_.\r\n\r\n*       *       *       *       *\r\n\r\nWhenever the train stops, I jump off, run to her carriage, and with\r\ndrawn cap await her orders. She wants coffee and then a glass of water,\r\nat another time a bowl of warm water to wash her hands, and thus it\r\ngoes on. She lets several men who have entered her compartment pay\r\ncourt to her. I am dying of jealousy and have to leap about like an\r\nantelope so as to secure what she wants quickly and not miss the train.\r\n\r\nIn this way the night passes. I haven\xe2\x80\x99t had time to eat a mouthful and\r\nI can\xe2\x80\x99t sleep, I have to breathe the same oniony air with Polish\r\npeasants, Jewish peddlers, and common soldiers.\r\n\r\nWhen I mount the steps of her coupe, she is lying stretched out on\r\ncushions in her comfortable furs, covered up with the skins of animals.\r\nShe is like an oriental despot, and the men sit like Indian deities,\r\nstraight upright against the walls and scarcely dare to breathe.\r\n\r\n*       *       *       *       *\r\n\r\nShe stops over in Vienna for a day to go shopping, and particularly to\r\nbuy series of luxurious gowns. She continues to treat me as her\r\nservant. I follow her at the respectful distance of ten paces. She\r\nhands me her packages without so much as even deigning a kind look, and\r\nladen down like a donkey I pant along behind.\r\n\r\nBefore leaving she takes all my clothes and gives them to the hotel\r\nwaiters. I am ordered to put on her livery. It is a Cracovian costume\r\nin her colors, light-blue with red facings, and red quadrangular cap,\r\nornamented with peacock-feathers. The costume is rather becoming to me.\r\n\r\nThe silver buttons bear her coat of arms. I have the feeling of having\r\nbeen sold or of having bonded myself to the devil. My fair demon leads\r\nme from Vienna to Florence. Instead of linen-garbed Mazovians and\r\ngreasy-haired Jews, my companions now are curly-haired Contadini, a\r\nmagnificent sergeant of the first Italian Grenadiers, and a poor German\r\npainter. The tobacco smoke no longer smells of onions, but of salami\r\nand cheese.\r\n\r\nNight has fallen again. I lie on my wooden bed as on a rack; my arms\r\nand legs seem broken. But there nevertheless is an element of poetry in\r\nthe affair. The stars sparkle round about, the Italian sergeant has a\r\nface like Apollo Belvedere, and the German painter sings a lovely\r\nGerman song.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cNow that all the shadows gather\r\nAnd endless stars grow light,\r\nDeep yearning on me falls\r\nAnd softly fills the night.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThrough the sea of dreams\r\nSailing without cease,\r\nSailing goes my soul\r\nIn thine to find release.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\r\nAnd I am thinking of the beautiful woman who is sleeping in regal\r\ncomfort among her soft furs.\r\n\r\n*       *       *       *       *\r\n\r\nFlorence! Crowds, cries, importunate porters and cab-drivers. Wanda\r\nchooses a carriage, and dismisses the porters.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhat have I a servant for,\xe2\x80\x9d she says, \xe2\x80\x9cGregor\xe2\x80\x94here is the ticket\xe2\x80\x94get\r\nthe luggage.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nShe wraps herself in her furs and sits quietly in the carriage while I\r\ndrag the heavy trunks hither, one after another. I break down for a\r\nmoment under the last one; a good-natured _carabiniere_ with an\r\nintelligent face comes to my assistance. She laughs.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cIt must be heavy,\xe2\x80\x9d said she, \xe2\x80\x9call my furs are in it.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nI get up on the driver\xe2\x80\x99s seat, wiping drops of perspiration from my\r\nbrow. She gives the name of the hotel, and the driver urges on his\r\nhorse. In a few minutes we halt at the brilliantly illuminated\r\nentrance.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cHave you any rooms?\xe2\x80\x9d she asks the portier.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYes, madame.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cTwo for me, one for my servant, all with stoves.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cTwo first-class rooms for you, madame, both with stoves,\xe2\x80\x9d replied the\r\nwaiter who had hastily come up, \xe2\x80\x9cand one without heat for your\r\nservant.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nShe looked at them, and then abruptly said: \xe2\x80\x9cthey are satisfactory,\r\nhave fires built at once; my servant can sleep in the unheated room.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nI merely looked at her.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cBring up the trunks, Gregor,\xe2\x80\x9d she commands, paying no attention to my\r\nlooks. \xe2\x80\x9cIn the meantime I\xe2\x80\x99ll be dressing, and then will go down to the\r\ndining-room, and you can eat something for supper.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nAs she goes into the adjoining room, I drag the trunks upstairs and\r\nhelp the waiter build a fire in her bed-room. He tries to question me\r\nin bad French about my employer. With a brief glance I see the blazing\r\nfire, the fragrant white poster-bed, and the rugs which cover the\r\nfloor. Tired and hungry I then descend the stairs, and ask for\r\nsomething to eat. A good-natured waiter, who used to be in the Austrian\r\narmy and takes all sorts of pains to entertain me in German, shows me\r\nthe dining-room and waits on me. I have just had the first fresh drink\r\nin thirty-six hours and the first bite of warm food on my fork, when\r\nshe enters.\r\n\r\nI rise.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhat do you mean by taking me into a dining-room in which my servant\r\nis eating,\xe2\x80\x9d she snaps at the waiter, flaring with anger. She turns\r\naround and leaves.\r\n\r\nMeanwhile I thank heaven that I am permitted to go on eating. Later I\r\nclimb the four flights upstairs to my room. My small trunk is already\r\nthere, and a miserable little oil-lamp is burning. It is a narrow room\r\nwithout fire-place, without a window, but with a small air-hole. If it\r\nweren\xe2\x80\x99t so beastly cold, it would remind me of one of the Venetian\r\n_piombi_.4 Involuntarily I have to laugh out aloud, so that it\r\nre-echoes, and I am startled by my own laughter.\r\n\r\n[Footnote 4: These were notorious prisons under the leaden roof of the\r\nPalace of the Doges.]\r\n\r\n\r\nSuddenly the door is pulled open and the waiter with a theatrical\r\nItalian gesture calls \xe2\x80\x9cYou are to come down to madame, at once.\xe2\x80\x9d I pick\r\nup my cap, stumble down the first few steps, but finally arrive in\r\nfront of her door on the first floor and knock.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cCome in!\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nI enter, shut the door, and stand attention.\r\n\r\nWanda has made herself comfortable. She is sitting in a neglige of\r\nwhite muslin and laces on a small red divan with her feet on a\r\nfootstool that matches. She has thrown her fur-cloak about her. It is\r\nthe identical cloak in which she appeared to me for the first time, as\r\ngoddess of love.\r\n\r\nThe yellow lights of the candelabra which stand on projections, their\r\nreflections in the large mirrors, and the red flames from the open\r\nfireplace play beautifully on the green velvet, the dark-brown sable of\r\nthe cloak, the smooth white skin, and the red, flaming hair of the\r\nbeautiful woman. Her clear, but cold face is turned toward me, and her\r\ncold green eyes rest upon me.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI am satisfied with you, Gregor,\xe2\x80\x9d she began.\r\n\r\nI bowed.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cCome closer.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nI obeyed.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cStill closer,\xe2\x80\x9d she looked down, and stroked the sable with her hand.\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cVenus in Furs receives her slave. I can see that you are more than an\r\nordinary dreamer, you don\xe2\x80\x99t remain far in arrears of your dreams; you\r\nare the sort of man who is ready to carry his dreams into effect, no\r\nmatter how mad they are. I confess, I like this; it impresses me. There\r\nis strength in this, and strength is the only thing one respects. I\r\nactually believe that under unusual circumstances, in a period of great\r\ndeeds, what seems to be your weakness would reveal itself as\r\nextraordinary power. Under the early emperors you would have been a\r\nmartyr, at the time of the Reformation an anabaptist, during the French\r\nRevolution one of those inspired Girondists who mounted the guillotine\r\nwith the marseillaise on their lips. But you are my slave, my\xe2\x80\x94\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nShe suddenly leaped up; the furs slipped down, and she threw her arms\r\nwith soft pressure about my neck.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cMy beloved slave, Severin, oh, how I love you, how I adore you, how\r\nhandsome you are in your Cracovian costume! You will be cold to-night\r\nup in your wretched room without a fire. Shall I give you one of my\r\nfurs, dear heart, the large one there\xe2\x80\x94\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nShe quickly picked it up, throwing it over my shoulders, and before I\r\nknew what had happened I was completely wrapped up in it.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cHow wonderfully becoming furs are to your face, they bring out your\r\nnoble lines. As soon as you cease being my slave, you must wear a\r\nvelvet coat with sable, do you understand? Otherwise I shall never put\r\non my fur-jacket again.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nAnd again she began to caress me and kiss me; finally she drew me down\r\non the little divan.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYou seem to be pleased with yourself in furs,\xe2\x80\x9d she said. \xe2\x80\x9cQuick,\r\nquick, give them to me, or I will lose all sense of dignity.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nI placed the furs about her, and Wanda slipped her right arm into the\r\nsleeve.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThis is the pose in Titian\xe2\x80\x99s picture.
