She looks on indifferently as he bleeds to death\r\nunder his opponent\xe2\x80\x99s claws, and follows the victor, the stronger\xe2\x80\x94that\r\nis the female\xe2\x80\x99s nature.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nAt this moment my lioness looked quickly and curiously at me.\r\n\r\nIt made me shudder, though I didn\xe2\x80\x99t know why\xe2\x80\x94and the red dawn immerses\r\nme and her and him in blood.\r\n\r\n*       *       *       *       *\r\n\r\nShe did not go to bed, but merely threw off her ball-dress and undid\r\nher hair; then she ordered me to build a fire, and she sat by the\r\nfire-place, and stared into the flames.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cDo you need me any longer, mistress?\xe2\x80\x9d I asked, my voice failed me at\r\nthe last word.\r\n\r\nWanda shook her head.\r\n\r\nI left the room, passed through the gallery, and sat down on one of the\r\nsteps, leading from there down into the garden. A gentle north wind\r\nbrought a fresh, damp coolness from the Arno, the green hills extended\r\ninto the distance in a rosy mist, a golden haze hovered over the city,\r\nover the round cupola of the Duomo.\r\n\r\nA few stars still tremble in the pale-blue sky.\r\n\r\nI tore open my coat, and pressed my burning forehead against the\r\nmarble. Everything that had happened so far seemed to me a mere child\xe2\x80\x99s\r\nplay; but now things were beginning to be serious, terribly serious.\r\n\r\nI anticipated a catastrophe, I visualized it, I could lay hold of it\r\nwith my hands, but I lacked the courage to meet it. My strength was\r\nbroken. And if I am honest with myself, neither the pains and\r\nsufferings that threatened me, not the humiliations that impended, were\r\nthe thing that frightened me.\r\n\r\nI merely felt a fear, the fear of losing her whom I loved with a sort\r\nof fanatical devotion; but it was so overwhelming, so crushing that I\r\nsuddenly began to sob like a child.\r\n\r\n*       *       *       *       *\r\n\r\nDuring the day she remained locked in her room, and had the negress\r\nattend her. When the evening star rose glowing in the blue sky, I saw\r\nher pass through the garden, and, carefully following her at a\r\ndistance, watched her enter the shrine of Venus. I stealthily followed\r\nand peered through the chink in the door.\r\n\r\nShe stood before the divine image of the goddess, her hands folded as\r\nin prayer, and the sacred light of the star of love casts its blue rays\r\nover her.\r\n\r\n*       *       *       *       *\r\n\r\nOn my couch at night the fear of losing her and despair took such\r\npowerful hold of me that they made a hero and a libertine of me. I\r\nlighted the little red oil-lamp which hung in the corridor beneath a\r\nsaint\xe2\x80\x99s image, and entered her bedroom, covering the light with one\r\nhand.\r\n\r\nThe lioness had been hunted and driven until she was exhausted. She had\r\nfallen asleep among her pillows, lying on her back, her hands clenched,\r\nbreathing heavily. A dream seemed to oppress her. I slowly withdrew my\r\nhand, and let the red light fall full on her wonderful face.\r\n\r\nBut she did not awaken.\r\n\r\nI gently set the lamp on the floor, sank down beside Wanda\xe2\x80\x99s bed, and\r\nrested my head on her soft, glowing arm.\r\n\r\nShe moved slightly, but even now did not awaken. I do not know how long\r\nI lay thus in the middle of the night, turned as into a stone by\r\nhorrible torments.\r\n\r\nFinally a severe trembling seized me, and I was able to cry. My tears\r\nflowed over her arm. She quivered several times and finally sat up; she\r\nbrushed her hand across her eyes, and looked at me.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cSeverin,\xe2\x80\x9d she exclaimed, more frightened than angry.\r\n\r\nI was unable to reply.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cSeverin,\xe2\x80\x9d she continued softly, \xe2\x80\x9cwhat is the matter? Are you ill?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nHer voice sounded so sympathetic, so kind, so full of love, that it\r\nclutched my breast like red-hot tongs and I began to sob aloud.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cSeverin,\xe2\x80\x9d she began anew. \xe2\x80\x9cMy poor unhappy friend.\xe2\x80\x9d Her hand gently\r\nstroked my hair. \xe2\x80\x9cI am sorry, very sorry for you; but I can\xe2\x80\x99t help you;\r\nwith the best intention in the world I know of nothing that would cure\r\nyou.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cOh, Wanda, must it be?\xe2\x80\x9d I moaned in my agony.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhat, Severin? What are you talking about?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cDon\xe2\x80\x99t you love me any more?\xe2\x80\x9d I continued. \xe2\x80\x9cHaven\xe2\x80\x99t you even a little\r\nbit of pity for me? Has the beautiful stranger taken complete\r\npossession of you?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI cannot lie,\xe2\x80\x9d she replied softly after a short pause. \xe2\x80\x9cHe has made an\r\nimpression on me which I haven\xe2\x80\x99t yet been able to analyse, further than\r\nthat I suffer and tremble beneath it. It is an impression of the sort I\r\nhave met with in the works of poets or on the stage, but I always\r\nthought it was a figment of the imagination. Oh, he is a man like a\r\nlion, strong and beautiful and yet gentle, not brutal like the men of\r\nour northern world. I am sorry for you, Severin, I am; but I must\r\npossess him. What am I saying? I must give myself to him, if he will\r\nhave me.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cConsider your reputation, Wanda, which so far has remained spotless,\xe2\x80\x9d\r\nI exclaimed, \xe2\x80\x9ceven if I no longer mean anything to you.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI am considering it,\xe2\x80\x9d she replied, \xe2\x80\x9cI intend to be strong, as long as\r\nit is possible, I want\xe2\x80\x94\xe2\x80\x9d she buried her head shyly in the pillows\xe2\x80\x94\xe2\x80\x9cI\r\nwant to become his wife\xe2\x80\x94if he will have me.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWanda,\xe2\x80\x9d I cried, seized again by that mortal fear, which always robs\r\nme of my breath, makes me lose possession of myself, \xe2\x80\x9cyou want to be\r\nhis wife, belong to him for always. Oh! Do not drive me away! He does\r\nnot love you\xe2\x80\x94\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWho says that?\xe2\x80\x9d she exclaimed, flaring up.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cHe does not love you,\xe2\x80\x9d I went on passionately, \xe2\x80\x9cbut I love you, I\r\nadore you, I am your slave, I let you tread me underfoot, I want to\r\ncarry you on my arms through life.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWho says that he doesn\xe2\x80\x99t love me?\xe2\x80\x9d she interrupted vehemently.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cOh! be mine,\xe2\x80\x9d I replied, \xe2\x80\x9cbe mine! I cannot exist, cannot live without\r\nyou. Have mercy on me, Wanda, have mercy!\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nShe looked at me again, and her face had her cold heartless expression,\r\nher evil smile.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYou say he doesn\xe2\x80\x99t love me,\xe2\x80\x9d she said, scornfully. \xe2\x80\x9cVery well then,\r\nget what consolation you can out of it.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nWith this she turned over on the other side, and contemptuously showed\r\nme her back.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cGood God, are you a woman without flesh or blood, haven\xe2\x80\x99t you a heart\r\nas well as I!\xe2\x80\x9d I cried, while my breast heaved convulsively.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYou know what I am,\xe2\x80\x9d she replied, coldly. \xe2\x80\x9cI am a woman of stone,\r\n_Venus in Furs_, your ideal, kneel down, and pray to me.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWanda!\xe2\x80\x9d I implored, \xe2\x80\x9cmercy!\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nShe began to laugh. I buried my face in her pillows. Pain had loosened\r\nthe floodgates of my tears and I let them flow.\r\n\r\nFor a long time silence reigned, then Wanda slowly raised herself.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYou bore me,\xe2\x80\x9d she began.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWanda!\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI am tired, let me go to sleep.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cMercy,\xe2\x80\x9d I implored. \xe2\x80\x9cDo not drive me away. No man, no one, will love\r\nyou as I do.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cLet me go to sleep,\xe2\x80\x9d\xe2\x80\x94she turned her back to me again.\r\n\r\nI leaped up, and snatched the poinard, which hung beside her bed, from\r\nits sheath, and placed its point against my breast.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI shall kill myself here before your eyes,\xe2\x80\x9d I murmured dully.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cDo what you please,\xe2\x80\x9d Wanda replied with complete indifference. \xe2\x80\x9cBut\r\nlet me go to sleep.\xe2\x80\x9d She yawned aloud. \xe2\x80\x9cI am very sleepy.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nFor a moment I stood as if petrified. Then I began to laugh and cry at\r\nthe same time. Finally I placed the poinard in my belt, and again fell\r\non my knees before her.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWanda, listen to me, only for a few moments,\xe2\x80\x9d I begged.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI want to go to sleep! Don\xe2\x80\x99t you hear!\xe2\x80\x9d she cried, leaping angrily out\r\nof bed and pushing me away with her foot. \xe2\x80\x9cYou forget that I am your\r\nmistress?\xe2\x80\x9d When I didn\xe2\x80\x99t budge, she seized the whip and struck me. I\r\nrose; she struck me again\xe2\x80\x94this time right in the face.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWretch, slave!\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nWith clenched fist held heavenward, I left her bedroom with a sudden\r\nresolve. She tossed the whip aside, and broke out into clear laughter.\r\nI can imagine that my theatrical attitude must have been very droll.\r\n\r\n*       *       *       *       *\r\n\r\nI have determined to set myself free from this heartless woman, who has\r\ntreated me so cruelly, and is now about to break faith and betray me,\r\nas a reward for all my slavish devotion, for everything I have suffered\r\nfrom her. I packed my few belongings into a bundle, and then wrote her\r\nas follows:\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cDear Madam,\xe2\x80\x94\r\n\r\nI have loved you even to madness, I have given myself to you as no man\r\never has given himself to a woman. You have abused my most sacred\r\nemotions, and played an impudent, frivolous game with me. However, as\r\nlong as you were merely cruel and merciless, it was still possible for\r\nme to love you. Now you are about to become _cheap_. I am no longer the\r\nslave whom you can kick about and whip. You yourself have set me free,\r\nand I am leaving a woman I can only hate and despise.\r\n\r\nSeverin Kusiemski.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nI handed these lines to the negress, and hastened away as fast as I\r\ncould go. I arrived at the railway-station all out of breath. Suddenly\r\nI felt a sharp pain in my heart and stopped. I began to weep. It is\r\nhumiliating that I want to flee and I can\xe2\x80\x99t. I turn back\xe2\x80\x94whither?\xe2\x80\x94to\r\nher, whom I abhor, and yet, at the same time, adore.\r\n\r\nAgain I pause. I cannot go back. I dare not.\r\n\r\nBut how am I to leave Florence. I remember that I haven\xe2\x80\x99t any money,\r\nnot a penny. Very well then, on foot; it is better to be an honest\r\nbeggar than to eat the bread of a courtesan.\r\n\r\nBut still I can\xe2\x80\x99t leave.\r\n\r\nShe has my pledge, my word of honor. I have to return. Perhaps she will\r\nrelease me.\r\n\r\nAfter a few rapid strides, I stop again.\r\n\r\nShe has my word of honor and my bond, that I shall remain her slave as\r\nlong as she desires, until she herself gives me my freedom. But I might\r\nkill myself.\r\n\r\nI go through the Cascine down to the Arno, where its yellow waters\r\nplash monotonously about a couple of stray willows. There I sit, and\r\ncast up my final accounts with existence. I let my entire life pass\r\nbefore me in review. On the whole, it is rather a wretched affair\xe2\x80\x94a few\r\njoys, an endless number of indifferent and worthless things, and\r\nbetween these an abundant harvest of pains, miseries, fears,\r\ndisappointments, shipwrecked hopes, afflictions, sorrow and grief.\r\n\r\nI thought of my mother, whom I loved so deeply and whom I had to watch\r\nwaste away beneath a horrible disease; of my brother, who full of the\r\npromise of joy and happiness died in the flower of youth, without even\r\nhaving put his lips to the cup of life. I thought of my dead nurse, my\r\nchildhood playmates, the friends that had striven and studied with me;\r\nof all those, covered by the cold, dead, indifferent earth. I thought\r\nof my turtle-dove, who not infrequently made his cooing bows to me,\r\ninstead of to his mate.\xe2\x80\x94All have returned, dust unto dust.\r\n\r\nI laughed aloud, and slid down into the water, but at the same moment I\r\ncaught hold of one of the willow-branches, hanging above the yellow\r\nwaves. As in a vision, I see the woman who has caused all my misery.\r\nShe hovers above the level of the water, luminous in the sunlight as\r\nthough she were transparent, with red flames about her head and neck.\r\nShe turns her face toward me and smiles.\r\n\r\n*       *       *       *       *\r\n\r\nI am back again, dripping, wet through, glowing with shame and fever.\r\nThe negress has delivered my letter; I am judged, lost, in the power of\r\na heartless, affronted woman.\r\n\r\nWell, let her kill me. I am unable to do it myself, and yet I have no\r\nwish to go on living.\r\n\r\nAs I walk around the house, she is standing in the gallery, leaning\r\nover the railing. Her face is full in the light of the sun, and her\r\ngreen eyes sparkle.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cStill alive?\xe2\x80\x9d she asked, without moving. I stood silent, with bowed\r\nhead.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cGive me back my poinard,\xe2\x80\x9d she continued. \xe2\x80\x9cIt is of no use to you. You\r\nhaven\xe2\x80\x99t even the courage to take your own life.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI have lost it,\xe2\x80\x9d I replied, trembling, shaken by chills.\r\n\r\nShe looked me over with a proud, scornful glance.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI suppose you lost it in the Arno?\xe2\x80\x9d She shrugged her shoulders. \xe2\x80\x9cNo\r\nmatter. Well, and why didn\xe2\x80\x99t you leave?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nI mumbled something which neither she nor I myself could understand.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cOh! you haven\xe2\x80\x99t any money,\xe2\x80\x9d she cried. \xe2\x80\x9cHere!\xe2\x80\x9d With an indescribably\r\ndisdainful gesture she tossed me her purse.\r\n\r\nI did not pick it up.\r\n\r\nBoth of us were silent for some time.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYou don\xe2\x80\x99t want to leave then?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI can\xe2\x80\x99t.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n*       *       *       *       *\r\n\r\nWanda drives in the Cascine without me, and goes to the theater without\r\nme; she receives company, and the negress serves her. No one asks after\r\nme. I stray about the garden, irresolutely, like an animal that has\r\nlost its master.\r\n\r\nLying among the bushes, I watch a couple of sparrows, fighting over a\r\nseed.\r\n\r\nSuddenly I hear the swish of a woman\xe2\x80\x99s dress.\r\n\r\nWanda approaches in a gown of dark silk, modestly closed up to the\r\nneck; the Greek is with her. They are in an eager discussion, but I\r\ncannot as yet understand a word of what they are saying. He stamps his\r\nfoot so that the gravel scatters about in all directions, and he lashes\r\nthe air with his riding whip. Wanda startles.\r\n\r\nIs she afraid that he will strike her?\r\n\r\nHave they gone that far?\r\n\r\nHe has left her, she calls him; he does not hear her, does not want to\r\nhear her.\r\n\r\nWanda sadly lowers her head, and then sits down on the nearest\r\nstone-bench. She sits for a long time, lost in thought. I watch her\r\nwith a sort of malevolent pleasure, finally I pull myself together by\r\nsheer force of will, and ironically step before her. She startles, and\r\ntrembles all over.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI come to wish you happiness,\xe2\x80\x9d I said, bowing, \xe2\x80\x9cI see, my dear lady,\r\ntoo, has found a master.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYes, thank God!\xe2\x80\x9d she exclaimed, \xe2\x80\x9cnot a new slave, I have had enough of\r\nthem. A master! Woman needs a master, and she adores him.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYou adore him, Wanda?\xe2\x80\x9d I cried, \xe2\x80\x9cthis brutal person\xe2\x80\x94\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYes, I love him, as I have never loved any one else.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWanda!\xe2\x80\x9d I clenched my fists, but tears already filled my eyes, and I\r\nwas seized by the delirium of passion, as by a sweet madness. \xe2\x80\x9cVery\r\nwell, take him as your husband, let him be your master, but I want to\r\nremain your slave, as long as I live.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYou want to remain my slave, even then?\xe2\x80\x9d she said, \xe2\x80\x9cthat would be\r\ninteresting, but I am afraid he wouldn\xe2\x80\x99t permit it.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cHe?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYes, he is already jealous of you,\xe2\x80\x9d she exclaimed, \xe2\x80\x9che, of you! He\r\ndemanded that I dismiss you immediately, and when I told him who you\r\nwere\xe2\x80\x94\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYou told him\xe2\x80\x94\xe2\x80\x9d I repeated, thunderstruck.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI told him everything,\xe2\x80\x9d she replied, \xe2\x80\x9cour whole story, all your\r\nqueerness, everything\xe2\x80\x94and he, instead of being amused, grew angry, and\r\nstamped his foot.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cAnd threatened to strike you?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nWanda looked to the ground, and remained silent.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYes, indeed,\xe2\x80\x9d I said with mocking bitterness, \xe2\x80\x9cyou are afraid of him,\r\nWanda!\xe2\x80\x9d I threw myself down at her feet, and in my agitation embraced\r\nher knees. \xe2\x80\x9cI don\xe2\x80\x99t want anything of you, except to be your slave, to\r\nbe always near you! I will be your dog-\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cDo you know, you bore me?\xe2\x80\x9d said Wanda, indifferently.\r\n\r\nI leaped up. Everything within me was seething.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYou are now no longer cruel, but cheap,\xe2\x80\x9d I said, clearly and\r\ndistinctly, accentuating every word.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYou have already written that in your letter,\xe2\x80\x9d Wanda replied, with a\r\nproud shrug of the shoulders. \xe2\x80\x9cA man of brains should never repeat\r\nhimself.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThe way you are treating me,\xe2\x80\x9d I broke out, \xe2\x80\x9cwhat would you call it?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI might punish you,\xe2\x80\x9d she replied ironically, \xe2\x80\x9cbut I prefer this time\r\nto reply with reasons instead of lashes. You have no right to accuse\r\nme. Haven\xe2\x80\x99t I always been honest with you? Haven\xe2\x80\x99t I warned you more\r\nthan once? Didn\xe2\x80\x99t I love you with all my heart, even passionately, and\r\ndid I conceal the fact from you, that it was dangerous to give yourself\r\ninto my power, to abase yourself before me, and that I want to be\r\ndominated? But you wished to be my plaything, my slave! You found the\r\nhighest pleasure in feeling the foot, the whip of an arrogant, cruel\r\nwoman. What do you want now?\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cDangerous potentialities were slumbering in me, but you were the first\r\nto awaken them. If I now take pleasure in torturing you, abusing you,\r\nit is your fault; you have made of me what I now am, and now you are\r\neven unmanly, weak, and miserable enough to accuse me.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYes, I am guilty,\xe2\x80\x9d I said, \xe2\x80\x9cbut haven\xe2\x80\x99t I suffered because of it? Let\r\nus put an end now to the cruel game.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThat is my wish, too,\xe2\x80\x9d she replied with a curious deceitful look.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWanda!\xe2\x80\x9d I exclaimed violently, \xe2\x80\x9cdon\xe2\x80\x99t drive me to extremes; you see\r\nthat I am a man again.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cA fire of straw,\xe2\x80\x9d she replied, \xe2\x80\x9cwhich makes a lot of stir for a\r\nmoment, and goes out as quickly as it flared up. You imagine you can\r\nintimidate me, and you only make yourself ridiculous. Had you been the\r\nman I first thought you were, serious, reserved, stern, I would have\r\nloved you faithfully, and become your wife. Woman demands that she can\r\nlook up to a man, but one like you who voluntarily places his neck\r\nunder her foot, she uses as a welcome plaything, only to toss it aside\r\nwhen she is tired of it.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cTry to toss me aside,\xe2\x80\x9d I said, jeeringly. \xe2\x80\x9cSome toys are dangerous.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cDon\xe2\x80\x99t challenge me,\xe2\x80\x9d exclaimed Wanda. Her eyes began to flash, and a\r\nflush entered her cheeks.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cIf you won\xe2\x80\x99t be mine now,\xe2\x80\x9d I continued, with a voice stifled with\r\nrage, \xe2\x80\x9cno one else shall possess you either.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhat play is this from?\xe2\x80\x9d she mocked, seizing me by the breast. She was\r\npale with anger at this moment. \xe2\x80\x9cDon\xe2\x80\x99t challenge me,\xe2\x80\x9d she continued, \xe2\x80\x9cI\r\nam not cruel, but I don\xe2\x80\x99t know whether I may not become so and whether\r\nthen there will be any bounds.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhat worse can you do, than to make your lover, your husband?\xe2\x80\x9d I\r\nexclaimed, more and more enraged.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI might make you _his_ slave,\xe2\x80\x9d she replied quickly, \xe2\x80\x9care you not in my\r\npower? Haven\xe2\x80\x99t I the agreement? But, of course, you will merely take\r\npleasure in it, if I have you bound, and say to him.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cDo with him what you please.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWoman, are you mad!\xe2\x80\x9d I cried.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI am entirely rational,\xe2\x80\x9d she said, calmly. \xe2\x80\x9cI warn you for the last\r\ntime. Don\xe2\x80\x99t offer any resistance, one who has gone as far as I have\r\ngone might easily go still further. I feel a sort of hatred for you,\r\nand would find a real joy in seeing him beat you to death; I am still\r\nrestraining myself, but\xe2\x80\x94\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nScarcely master of myself any longer, I seized her by the wrist and\r\nforced her to the ground, so that she lay on her knees before me.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cSeverin!\xe2\x80\x9d she cried. Rage and terror were painted on her face.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI shall kill you if you marry him,\xe2\x80\x9d I threatened; the words came\r\nhoarsely and dully from my breast. \xe2\x80\x9cYou are mine, I won\xe2\x80\x99t let you go, I\r\nlove you too much.\xe2\x80\x9d Then I clutched her and pressed her close to me; my\r\nright hand involuntarily seized the dagger which I still had in my\r\nbelt.\r\n\r\nWanda fixed a large, calm, incomprehensible look on me.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI like you that way,\xe2\x80\x9d she said, carelessly. \xe2\x80\x9cNow you are a man, and at\r\nthis moment I know I still love you.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWanda,\xe2\x80\x9d I wept with rapture, and bent down over her, covering her dear\r\nface with kisses, and she, suddenly breaking into a loud gay laugh,\r\nsaid, \xe2\x80\x9cHave you finished with your ideal now, are you satisfied with\r\nme?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYou mean?\xe2\x80\x9d I stammered, \xe2\x80\x9cthat you weren\xe2\x80\x99t serious?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI am very serious,\xe2\x80\x9d she gaily continued. \xe2\x80\x9cI love you, only you, and\r\nyou\xe2\x80\x94you foolish, little man, didn\xe2\x80\x99t know that everything was only\r\nmake-believe and play-acting. How hard it often was for me to strike\r\nyou with the whip, when I would have rather taken your head and covered\r\nit with kisses. But now we are through with that, aren\xe2\x80\x99t we? I have\r\nplayed my cruel role better than you expected, and now you will be\r\nsatisfied with my being a good, little wife who isn\xe2\x80\x99t altogether\r\nunattractive. Isn\xe2\x80\x99t that so? We will live like rational people\xe2\x80\x94\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYou will marry me!\xe2\x80\x9d I cried, overflowing with happiness.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYes\xe2\x80\x94marry you\xe2\x80\x94you dear, darling man,\xe2\x80\x9d whispered Wanda, kissing my\r\nhands.\r\n\r\nI drew her up to my breast.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cNow, you are no longer Gregor, my slave,\xe2\x80\x9d said she, \xe2\x80\x9cbut Severin, the\r\ndear man I love\xe2\x80\x94\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cAnd he\xe2\x80\x94you don\xe2\x80\x99t love him?\xe2\x80\x9d I asked in agitation.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cHow could you imagine my loving a man of his brutal type? You were\r\nblind to everything, I was really afraid for you.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI almost killed myself for your sake.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cReally?\xe2\x80\x9d she cried, \xe2\x80\x9cah, I still tremble at the thought, that you were\r\nalready in the Arno.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cBut you saved me,\xe2\x80\x9d I replied, tenderly. \xe2\x80\x9cYou hovered over the waters\r\nand smiled, and your smile called me back to life.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n*       *       *       *       *\r\n\r\nI have a curious feeling when I now hold her in my arms and she lies\r\nsilently against my breast and lets me kiss her and smiles. I feel like\r\none who has suddenly awakened out of a feverish delirium, or like a\r\nshipwrecked man who has for many days battled with waves that\r\nmomentarily threatened to devour him and finally has found a safe\r\nshore.\r\n\r\n*       *       *       *       *\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI hate this Florence, where you have been so unhappy,\xe2\x80\x9d she declared,\r\nas I was saying good-night to her. \xe2\x80\x9cI want to leave immediately,\r\ntomorrow, you will be good enough to write a couple of letters for me,\r\nand, while you are doing that, I will drive to the city to pay my\r\nfarewell visits. Is that satisfactory to you?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cOf course, you dear, sweet, beautiful woman.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n*       *       *       *       *\r\n\r\nEarly in the morning she knocked at my door to ask how I had slept. Her\r\ntenderness is positively wonderful. I should never have believed that\r\nshe could be so tender.\r\n\r\n*       *       *       *       *\r\n\r\nShe has now been gone for over four hours. I have long since finished\r\nthe letters, and am now sitting in the gallery, looking down the street\r\nto see whether I cannot discover her carriage in the distance. I am a\r\nlittle worried about her, and yet I know there is no reason under\r\nheaven why I should doubt or fear. However, a feeling of oppression\r\nweighs me down, and I cannot rid myself of it. It is probably the\r\nsufferings of the past days, which still cast their shadows into my\r\nsoul.\r\n\r\n*       *       *       *       *\r\n\r\nShe is back, radiant with happiness and contentment.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWell, has everything gone as you wished?\xe2\x80\x9d I asked tenderly, kissing\r\nher hand.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYes, dear heart,\xe2\x80\x9d she replied, \xe2\x80\x9cand we shall leave to-night. Help me\r\npack my trunks.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n*       *       *       *       *\r\n\r\nToward evening she asked me to go to the post-office and mail her\r\nletters myself. I took her carriage, and was back within an hour.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cMistress has asked for you,\xe2\x80\x9d said the negress, with a grin, as I\r\nascended the wide marble stairs.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cHas anyone been here?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cNo one,\xe2\x80\x9d she replied, crouching down on the steps like a black cat.\r\n\r\nI slowly passed through the drawing-room, and then stood before her\r\nbedroom door.\r\n\r\nWhy does my heart beat so? Am I not perfectly happy?\r\n\r\nOpening the door softly, I draw back the portiere. Wanda is lying on\r\nthe ottoman, and does not seem to notice me. How beautiful she looks,\r\nin her silver-gray dress, which fits closely, and while displaying in\r\ntell-tale fashion her splendid figure, leaves her wonderful bust and\r\narms bare.\r\n\r\nHer hair is interwoven with, and held up by a black velvet ribbon. A\r\nmighty fire is burning in the fire-place, the hanging lamp casts a\r\nreddish glow, and the whole room is as if drowned in blood.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWanda,\xe2\x80\x9d I said at last.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cOh Severin,\xe2\x80\x9d she cried out joyously. \xe2\x80\x9cI have been impatiently waiting\r\nfor you.\xe2\x80\x9d She leaped up, and folded me in her arms. She sat down again\r\non the rich cushions and tried to draw me down to her side, but I\r\nsoftly slid down to her feet and placed my head in her lap.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cDo you know I am very much in love with you to-day?\xe2\x80\x9d she whispered,\r\nbrushing a few stray hairs from my forehead and kissing my eyes.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cHow beautiful your eyes are, I have always loved them as the best of\r\nyou, but to-day they fairly intoxicate me. I am all\xe2\x80\x94\xe2\x80\x9d She extended her\r\nmagnificent limbs and tenderly looked at me from beneath her red\r\nlashes.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cAnd you\xe2\x80\x94you are cold\xe2\x80\x94you hold me like a block of wood; wait, I\xe2\x80\x99ll stir\r\nyou with the fire of love,\xe2\x80\x9d she said, and again clung fawningly and\r\ncaressingly to my lips.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI no longer please you; I suppose I\xe2\x80\x99ll have to be cruel to you again,\r\nevidently I have been too kind to you to-day. Do you know, you little\r\nfool, what I shall do, I shall whip you for a while\xe2\x80\x94\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cBut child\xe2\x80\x94\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI want to.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWanda!\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cCome, let me bind you,\xe2\x80\x9d she continued, and ran gaily through the room.\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI want to see you very much in love, do you understand? Here are the\r\nropes. I wonder if I can still do it?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nShe began with fettering my feet and then she tied my hands behind my\r\nback, pinioning my arms like those of a prisoner.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cSo,\xe2\x80\x9d she said, with gay eagerness. \xe2\x80\x9cCan you still move?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cNo.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cFine\xe2\x80\x94\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nShe then tied a noose in a stout rope, threw it over my head, and let\r\nit slip down as far as the hips. She drew it tight, and bound me to a\r\npillar.\r\n\r\nA curious tremor seized me at that moment.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI have a feeling as if I were about to be executed,\xe2\x80\x9d I said with a low\r\nvoice.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWell, you shall have a thorough punishment to-day,\xe2\x80\x9d exclaimed Wanda.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cBut put on your fur-jacket, please,\xe2\x80\x9d I said.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI shall gladly give you that pleasure,\xe2\x80\x9d she replied. She got her\r\n_kazabaika_, and put it on. Then she stood in front of me with her arms\r\nfolded across her chest, and looked at me out of half-closed eyes.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cDo you remember the story of the ox of Dionysius?\xe2\x80\x9d she asked.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI remember it only vaguely, what about it?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cA courtier invented a new implement of torture for the Tyrant of\r\nSyracuse. It was an iron ox in which those condemned to death were to\r\nbe shut, and then pushed into a mighty furnace.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cAs soon as the iron ox began to get hot, and the condemned person\r\nbegan to cry out in his torment, his wails sounded like the bellowing\r\nof an ox.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cDionysius nodded graciously to the inventor, and to put his invention\r\nto an immediate test had him shut up in the iron ox.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cIt is a very instructive story.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cIt was you who innoculated me with selfishness, pride, and cruelty,\r\nand _you shall be their first victim._ I now literally enjoy having a\r\nhuman being that thinks and feels and desires like myself in my power;\r\nI love to abuse a man who is stronger in intelligence and body than I,\r\nespecially a man who loves me.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cDo you still love me?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cEven to madness,\xe2\x80\x9d I exclaimed.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cSo much the better,\xe2\x80\x9d she replied, \xe2\x80\x9cand so much the more will you enjoy\r\nwhat I am about to do with you now.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhat is the matter with you?\xe2\x80\x9d I asked. \xe2\x80\x9cI don\xe2\x80\x99t understand you, there\r\nis a gleam of real cruelty in your eyes to-day, and you are strangely\r\nbeautiful\xe2\x80\x94completely _Venus in Furs.\xe2\x80\x9d_\r\n\r\nWithout replying Wanda placed her arms around my neck and kissed me. I\r\nwas again seized by my fanatical passion.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhere is the whip?\xe2\x80\x9d I asked.\r\n\r\nWanda laughed, and withdrew a couple of steps.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYou really insist upon being punished?\xe2\x80\x9d she exclaimed, proudly tossing\r\nback her head.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYes.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nSuddenly Wanda\xe2\x80\x99s face was completely transformed. It was as if\r\ndisfigured by rage; for a moment she seemed even ugly to me.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cVery well, then _you_ whip him!\xe2\x80\x9d she called loudly.\r\n\r\nAt the same instant the beautiful Greek stuck his head of black curls\r\nthrough the curtains of her four-poster bed. At first I was speechless,\r\npetrified. There was a horribly comic element in the situation. I would\r\nhave laughed aloud, had not my position been at the same time so\r\nterribly cruel and humiliating.\r\n\r\nIt went beyond anything I had imagined. A cold shudder ran down my\r\nback, when my rival stepped from the bed in his riding boots, his\r\ntight-fitting white breeches, and his short velvet jacket, and I saw\r\nhis athletic limbs.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYou are indeed cruel,\xe2\x80\x9d he said, turning to Wanda.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cOnly inordinately fond of pleasure,\xe2\x80\x9d she replied with a wild sort of\r\nhumor. \xe2\x80\x9cPleasure alone lends value to existence; whoever enjoys does\r\nnot easily part from life, whoever suffers or is needy meets death like\r\na friend.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cBut whoever wants to enjoy must take life gaily in the sense of the\r\nancient world; he dare not hesitate to enjoy at the expense of others;\r\nhe must never feel pity; he must be ready to harness others to his\r\ncarriage or his plough as though they were animals. He must know how to\r\nmake slaves of men who feel and would enjoy as he does, and use them\r\nfor his service and pleasure without remorse. It is not his affair\r\nwhether they like it, or whether they go to rack and ruin. He must\r\nalways remember this, that if they had him in their power, as he has\r\nthem they would act in exactly the same way, and he would have to pay\r\nfor their pleasure with his sweat and blood and soul. That was the\r\nworld of the ancients: pleasure and cruelty, liberty and slavery went\r\nhand in hand. People who want to live like the gods of Olympus must of\r\nnecessity have slaves whom they can toss into their fish-ponds, and\r\ngladiators who will do battle, the while they banquet, and they must\r\nnot mind if by chance a bit of blood bespatters them.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nHer words brought back my complete self-possession.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cUnloosen me!\xe2\x80\x9d I exclaimed angrily.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cAren\xe2\x80\x99t you my slave, my property?\xe2\x80\x9d replied Wanda. \xe2\x80\x9cDo you want me to\r\nshow you the agreement?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cUntie me!\xe2\x80\x9d I threatened, \xe2\x80\x9cotherwise\xe2\x80\x94\xe2\x80\x9d I tugged at the ropes.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cCan he tear himself free?\xe2\x80\x9d she asked. \xe2\x80\x9cHe has threatened to kill me.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cBe entirely at ease,\xe2\x80\x9d said the Greek, testing my fetters.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI shall call for help,\xe2\x80\x9d I began again.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cNo one will hear you,\xe2\x80\x9d replied Wanda, \xe2\x80\x9cand no one will hinder me from\r\nabusing your most sacred emotions or playing a frivolous game with\r\nyou.\xe2\x80\x9d she continued, repeating with satanic mockery phrases from my\r\nletter to her.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cDo you think I am at this moment merely cruel and merciless, or am I\r\nalso about to become cheap? What? Do you still love me, or do you\r\nalready hate and despise me? Here is the whip\xe2\x80\x94\xe2\x80\x9d She handed it to the\r\nGreek who quickly stepped closer.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cDon\xe2\x80\x99t you dare!\xe2\x80\x9d I exclaimed, trembling with indignation, \xe2\x80\x9cI won\xe2\x80\x99t\r\npermit it\xe2\x80\x94\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cOh, because I don\xe2\x80\x99t wear furs,\xe2\x80\x9d the Greek replied with an ironical\r\nsmile, and he took his short sable from the bed.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYou are adorable,\xe2\x80\x9d exclaimed Wanda, kissing him, and helping him into\r\nhis furs.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cMay I really whip him?\xe2\x80\x9d he asked.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cDo with him what you please,\xe2\x80\x9d replied Wanda.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cBeast!\xe2\x80\x9d I exclaimed, utterly revolted.\r\n\r\nThe Greek fixed his cold tigerish look upon me and tried out the whip.\r\nHis muscles swelled when he drew back his arms, and made the whip hiss\r\nthrough the air. I was bound like Marsyas while Apollo was getting\r\nready to flay me.\r\n\r\nMy look wandered about the room and remained fixed on the ceiling,\r\nwhere Samson, lying at Delilah\xe2\x80\x99s feet, was about to have his eyes put\r\nout by the Philistines. The picture at that moment seemed to me like a\r\nsymbol, an eternal parable of passion and lust, of the love of man for\r\nwoman. \xe2\x80\x9cEach one of us in the end is a Samson,\xe2\x80\x9d I thought, \xe2\x80\x9cand\r\nultimately for better or worse is betrayed by the woman he loves,\r\nwhether he wears an ordinary coat or sables.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cNow watch me break him in,\xe2\x80\x9d said the Greek. He showed his teeth, and\r\nhis face acquired the blood-thirsty expression, which startled me the\r\nfirst time I saw him.\r\n\r\nAnd he began to apply the lash\xe2\x80\x94so mercilessly, with such frightful\r\nforce that I quivered under each blow, and began to tremble all over\r\nwith pain. Tears rolled down over my cheeks. In the meantime Wanda lay\r\non the ottoman in her fur-jacket, supporting herself on her arm; she\r\nlooked on with cruel curiosity, and was convulsed with laughter.\r\n\r\nThe sensation of being whipped by a successful rival before the eyes of\r\nan adored woman cannot be described. I almost went mad with shame and\r\ndespair.\r\n\r\nWhat was most humiliating was that at first I felt a certain wild,\r\nsupersensual stimulation under Apollo\xe2\x80\x99s whip and the cruel laughter of\r\nmy Venus, no matter how horrible my position was. But Apollo whipped on\r\nand on, blow after blow, until I forgot all about poetry, and finally\r\ngritted my teeth in impotent rage, and cursed my wild dreams, woman,\r\nand love.\r\n\r\nAll of a sudden I saw with horrible clarity whither blind passion and\r\nlust have led man, ever since Holofernes and Agamemnon\xe2\x80\x94into a blind\r\nalley, into the net of woman\xe2\x80\x99s treachery, into misery, slavery, and\r\ndeath.\r\n\r\nIt was as though I were awakening from a dream.\r\n\r\nBlood was already flowing under the whip. I wound like a worm that is\r\ntrodden on, but he whipped on without mercy, and she continued to laugh\r\nwithout mercy. In the meantime she locked her packed trunk and slipped\r\ninto her travelling furs, and was still laughing, when she went\r\ndownstairs on his arm and entered the carriage.\r\n\r\nThen everything was silent for a moment.\r\n\r\nI listened breathlessly.\r\n\r\nThe carriage door slammed, the horse began to pull\xe2\x80\x94the rolling of the\r\ncarriage for a short time\xe2\x80\x94then all was over.\r\n\r\n*       *       *       *       *\r\n\r\nFor a moment I thought of taking vengeance, of killing him, but I was\r\nbound by the abominable agreement. So nothing was left for me to do\r\nexcept to keep my pledged word and grit my teeth.\r\n\r\n*       *       *       *       *\r\n\r\nMy first impulse after this, the most cruel catastrophe of my life, was\r\nto seek laborious tasks, dangers, and privations. I wanted to become a\r\nsoldier and go to Asia or Algiers, but my father was old and ill and\r\nwanted me.\r\n\r\nSo I quietly returned home and for two years helped him bear his\r\nburdens, and learned how to look after the estate which I had never\r\ndone before. To _labor_ and to _do my duty_ was comforting like a drink\r\nof fresh water. Then my father died, and I inherited the estate, but it\r\nmeant no change.\r\n\r\nI had put on my own Spanish boots and went on living just as rationally\r\nas if the old man were standing behind me, looking over my shoulder\r\nwith his large wise eyes.\r\n\r\nOne day a box arrived, accompanied by a letter. I recognized Wanda\xe2\x80\x99s\r\nwriting.\r\n\r\nCuriously moved, I opened it, and read.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cSir.\xe2\x80\x94\r\n\r\nNow that over three years have passed since that night in Florence, I\r\nsuppose, I may confess to you that I loved you deeply. You yourself,\r\nhowever, stifled my love by your fantastic devotion and your insane\r\npassion. From the moment that you became my slave, I knew it would be\r\nimpossible for you ever to become my husband. However, I found it\r\ninteresting to have you realize your ideal in my own person, and, while\r\nI gloriously amused myself, perhaps, to cure you.\r\n\r\nI found the strong man for whom I felt a need, and I was as happy with\r\nhim as, I suppose, it is possible for any one to be on this funny ball\r\nof clay.\r\n\r\nBut my happiness, like all things mortal, was of short duration. About\r\na year ago he fell in a duel, and since then I have been living in\r\nParis, like an Aspasia\xe2\x80\x94\r\n\r\nAnd you?\xe2\x80\x94Your life surely is not without its sunshine, if you have\r\ngained control of your imagination, and those qualities in you have\r\nmaterialized, which at first so attracted me to you\xe2\x80\x94your clarity of\r\nintellect, kindness of heart, and, above all else, your\xe2\x80\x94_moral\r\nseriousness_.\r\n\r\nI hope you have been cured under my whip; the cure was cruel, but\r\nradical. In memory of that time and of a woman who loved you\r\npassionately, I am sending you the portrait by the poor German.\r\n\r\n_Venus in Furs_.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nI had to smile, and as I fell to musing the beautiful woman suddenly\r\nstood before me in her velvet jacket trimmed with ermine, with the whip\r\nin her hand. And I continued to smile at the woman I had once loved so\r\ninsanely, at the fur-jacket that had once so entranced me, at the whip,\r\nand ended by smiling at myself and saying: The cure was cruel, but\r\nradical; but the main point is, I have been cured.\r\n\r\n*       *       *       *       *\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cAnd the moral of the story?\xe2\x80\x9d I said to Severin when I put the\r\nmanuscript down on the table.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThat I was a donkey,\xe2\x80\x9d he exclaimed without turning around, for he\r\nseemed to be embarrassed. \xe2\x80\x9cIf only I had beaten her!\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cA curious remedy,\xe2\x80\x9d I exclaimed, \xe2\x80\x9cwhich might answer with your\r\npeasant-women\xe2\x80\x94\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cOh, they are used to it,\xe2\x80\x9d he replied eagerly, \xe2\x80\x9cbut imagine the effect\r\nupon one of our delicate, nervous, hysterical ladies\xe2\x80\x94\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cBut the moral?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThat woman, as nature has created her and as man is at present\r\neducating her, is his enemy. She can only be his slave or his despot,\r\nbut _never his companion._ This she can become only when she has the\r\nsame rights as he, and is his equal in education and work.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cAt present we have only the choice of being hammer or anvil, and I was\r\nthe kind of donkey who let a woman make a slave of him, do you\r\nunderstand?\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThe moral of the tale is this: whoever allows himself to be whipped,\r\ndeserves to be whipped.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThe blows, as you see, have agreed with me; the roseate supersensual\r\nmist has dissolved, and no one can ever make me believe again that\r\nthese \xe2\x80\x98sacred apes of Benares\xe2\x80\x996 or Plato\xe2\x80\x99s rooster7  are the image of\r\nGod.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n[Footnote 6: One of Schopenhauer\xe2\x80\x99s designations for women.]\r\n\r\n\r\n[Footnote 7: Diogenes threw a plucked rooster into Plato\xe2\x80\x99s school and\r\nexclaimed: \xe2\x80\x9cHere you have Plato\xe2\x80\x99s human being.\xe2\x80\x9d]\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n*** END OF THE PROJECT GUTENBERG EBOOK VENUS IN FURS ***\r\n\r\nUpdated editions will replace the previous one--the old editions will\r\nbe renamed.\r\n\r\nCreating the works from print editions not protected by U.S. copyright\r\nlaw means that no one owns a United States copyright in these works,\r\nso the Foundation (and you!) can copy and distribute it in the\r\nUnited States without permission and without paying copyright\r\nroyalties.
